- **Facts that reshaped the design (all `[verified: sonnet-5]` unless noted):**
  1. **Inbound routing is exact-source-address match, pre-crypto.** `process_inbound_ciphertext` maps `remote_addr` → peer via `find_node_id_by_endpoint` (`engine.rs:372-377`, exact `SocketAddr` equality); an unmatched source is dropped at `engine.rs:268-270` **before any `decapsulate`** — no receiver-index routing exists, and there is no roaming: `peer_state.endpoint` is written only by `configure_peer` (`engine.rs:172`) and `update_peer_endpoint` (`engine.rs:189`); the backend declares `supports_roaming: false` (`userspace_shared/mod.rs:388-396`).
  2. **The round-trip primitive was deliberately shaped to never talk to peers.** It is a per-runtime SINGLETON (`outstanding_round_trip: Option<_>`), matched by **source address only** (`try_deliver_round_trip_response`, `runtime.rs:782-795`), and `reject_round_trip_target` (`runtime.rs:772-780`) refuses any target matching a configured peer endpoint `[verified: first-hand read]`.
  3. **The race flips the live endpoint on EVERY probe attempt.** `Phase10PeerRuntime::send_probe` (`phase10.rs:98-109`) calls `reconfigure_managed_peer` (→ `backend.update_peer_endpoint`, `phase10.rs:5907`) for each probed pair before initiating the handshake — not just for the winner.
  4. **A fresh-handshake short-circuit would neutralize a naive forced re-race:** `traversal_probe_uses_existing_fresh_handshake_on_current_endpoint` (`phase10.rs:10545`) pins that a fresh current-endpoint handshake returns `Direct`/`ExistingFreshHandshake` with 0 attempts — exactly the degraded-but-fresh case this proposal targets. The demotion seam must bypass it explicitly.
  5. **No deprioritization seam exists today:** `execute_ice_pair_race` (`traversal.rs:1402-1414`) and `generate_candidate_pairs` (`ice_priority.rs:313-317`) expose no exclusion/penalty parameter; pairs are RFC-8445-priority sorted (`ice_priority.rs:288`), capped at 32 (`ice_priority.rs:305`) then `max_probe_pairs` (`traversal.rs:1462`).
  6. **`force_reprobe` is global-per-invocation, never per-peer:** single `traversal_probe_due` call site (`daemon.rs:5768` in `sync_traversal_runtime_state` :5613), fed by hardcoded literals at each `refresh_traversal_hint_state` caller (bootstrap :6796/:6922, IPC Netcheck :7255 true / Status :7033 false / StateRefresh :7259, pre-expiry :4757, endpoint-change :4844, reconcile :8190 false). A per-peer trigger is new state.
  7. **The reconcile cadence is 1s** (`DEFAULT_RECONCILE_INTERVAL_MS = 1_000`, `daemon.rs:322`; `reconcile()` :8106 calls `refresh_traversal_hint_state(false)` at :8190 every tick).
  8. **`TraversalProbeStatus` is rebuilt from scratch every sync pass** (`daemon.rs:5911` replaces the whole map) — any cross-pass EWMA/dwell state MUST live in a separate map. (Coordination note for FIS-0010: its three added fields hit the same rebuild and need explicit carry-over.)
  9. **Status-line telemetry is safe to extend:** the format-pinning assertions (`daemon.rs:20605`, `:20696`, both inside `daemon_runtime_auto_tunnel_traversal_probe_falls_back_to_relay_without_handshake_evidence` :20457) are substring `.contains("key=value")` checks — added fields break nothing.
  10. **Dyn-compatibility must hold:** `TunnelBackend` is used as `&mut dyn TunnelBackend` throughout the contract suites (`backend_contract.rs:203` + 20 `contract_*` fns; `stub_conformance.rs:61+`); production holds it generically (`Phase10Controller<B: TunnelBackend, _>`, `phase10.rs:4803`).

- **The shadow probe is dropped — resolution of FIS-0001's weakest part:** all three transport variants fail against the verified code, so the alternate path is never measured remotely; instead, sustained measured degradation of the CURRENT path triggers the existing authenticated race with the incumbent demoted. The WG handshake — Noise-authenticated, unforgeable off-path — is the only path-validation signal (this is the QUIC RFC 9000 §9 probe-before-commit *shape* implemented with WireGuard's native primitive; the honest deviation, inherited from fact 3, is that probing itself flips the live endpoint slot — bounded-blip, not make-before-break; the "make-before-break" label in FIS-0001's title is hereby retired). Per-variant kill rationale is in Considered-and-rejected.
  **Numbered acceptance criteria (supersedes review fix #2's nonce requirement — stronger, structural):**
  1. No new unauthenticated network input, listener, or responder is introduced anywhere; path selection consumes only (a) WireGuard's authenticated counters/handshakes and (b) locally-computed arithmetic over them.
  2. A path commit occurs only via the existing race decision arms, gated on an authenticated handshake advance; an off-path attacker who can forge arbitrary UDP cannot influence the degradation verdict (loss derives from authenticated receive counters, RTT from authenticated handshake round-trips) nor the race outcome (Noise MACs) — forced-flap-on-a-timer is structurally excluded, not rate-limited away.

- **Named mechanism (post-fix per review fix #1):** **EWMA + fixed-margin threshold + dwell-time hysteresis** feeding a **degradation-triggered forced re-race with incumbent demotion**. No CUSUM (at ≤1 RTT sample per ~120s rekey there is no detection-power argument for it — Considered-and-rejected). RFC 6298 is borrowed ONLY for the SRTT/RTTVAR smoothing constants alpha=1/8, beta=1/4 — none of its RTO/backoff semantics (review fix #4).

  1. **One shared sampling layer (FIS-0004 reads this):** new module `crates/rustynetd/src/path_quality.rs`, owning `PathQualityTracker { peers: BTreeMap<NodeId, PathQualityState> }` — a daemon-side map SEPARATE from `traversal_probe_statuses` (forced by fact 8). `PathQualityState { srtt_ms: f32, rttvar_ms: f32, srtt_slow_ms: f32, loss_ewma: f32, rtt_samples: u8, degraded_streak: u8, last_ingest_handshake_unix: Option<u64>, last_sample_unix: u64, last_quality_rerace_unix: u64 }` — all primitives, ~48 B/peer. FIS-0004's relay-preference accelerant becomes a reader of this tracker; FIS-0004's opt-in pacing gate (its Phase 4) consumes a daemon-pushed per-peer hint at the same 1s cadence rather than computing its own in-pump estimate — one smoothing layer, two consumers, and the pump gains no sampling work (FIS-0012 boundary respected: nothing here runs per-packet or per-10ms-tick).
  2. **EWMA home = daemon-side.** Justification (this was §-open-point 1): (a) fact 8 forces a dedicated cross-pass map in the daemon anyway; (b) the exact precedent is `peer_latest_handshake_unix` — raw primitive up, judgment (freshness) in the daemon; (c) the decision inputs it must compose with (dwell, FIS-0010 breaker, candidate sets) are all daemon-side; (d) backend stays a dumb measurement source, so command-only backends are `Ok(None)` by default with zero code.
  3. **Trait extension (§-open-point 2), mirroring `peer_latest_handshake_unix`'s `Result<Option<_>>` shape (`lib.rs:184-185`), default body, dyn-compatible:**

  ```rust
  // rustynet-backend-api/src/lib.rs — primitive-only (review fix #3): u32/f32/u64,
  // no boringtun type or concept crosses; PartialEq only (f32 ⇒ no Eq, unlike TunnelStats).
  #[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq)]
  pub struct PeerPathSample {
      pub rtt_ms: Option<u32>,               // last handshake round-trip; sticky between handshakes
      pub loss_ratio: f32,                   // 0.0..=1.0, backend's own smoothed estimate
      pub latest_handshake_unix: Option<u64>,// epoch marker for RTT dedup
      pub tx_bytes: u64,
      pub rx_bytes: u64,
  }
  fn peer_path_sample(&mut self, _node_id: &NodeId)
      -> Result<Option<PeerPathSample>, BackendError> { Ok(None) }
  ```

  Backend plumbing copies the verified `peer_latest_handshake_unix` chain (`mod.rs:453-458` → `RuntimeControl` `runtime.rs:188-193` → `request()` :334-345 → `RuntimeRequest::PeerLatestHandshake` :363-366 → worker arm :1016-1019 `[verified: sonnet-5]`): new `RuntimeRequest::PeerPathSample { node_id, reply }`, worker arm reads the peer's `Tunn::stats()` via a new engine accessor `pub(crate) fn peer_path_sample(&self, node_id: &NodeId) -> Option<PeerPathSample>` (the actual un-discard — a new consuming accessor; the two existing discard sites stay untouched, correctly, since their callers don't need loss/rtt) plus `handshake_telemetry.latest_handshake`. The engine lands once (macOS shares engine.rs); the macOS runtime needs its own mirrored request variant + arm (same shape as FIS-0012's mirror commits). Command-only backends compile unchanged and return the fail-closed no-data default.
  4. **Ingest at the 1s reconcile tick (fact 7), never in the pump:** for each `PathMode::Direct` managed peer, `backend.peer_path_sample(...)`; RTT is ingested only when `latest_handshake_unix` advanced past `last_ingest_handshake_unix` (dedups the sticky `last_rtt` — without this, the EWMA collapses onto one repeated sample); `srtt/rttvar` update with 1/8, 1/4; `srtt_slow_ms` (alpha=1/64) is the drift baseline; `loss_ewma ← 0.75·loss_ewma + 0.25·loss_ratio` (light re-smoothing of boringtun's already-session-weighted estimator, damping rekey-boundary steps — double-smoothing acknowledged and deliberate).
  5. **Verdict — pure function, fail-closed (§-open-point 4 constants + noise arguments):** `Insufficient` (⇒ keep current path, no recommendation) unless `rtt_samples ≥ 2` AND `now − last_sample_unix ≤ 10s`. `Degraded` iff sustained — `degraded_streak ≥ 5` consecutive 1s polls — on either arm: **loss arm** `loss_ewma ≥ 0.05` (5%: home-Wi-Fi baseline is <1%, FIS-0004's 2% is its *advisory* accelerant threshold; an endpoint flip is more disruptive than a reprobe accelerant so it takes the higher bar); **rtt arm** `srtt ≥ 2·srtt_slow AND srtt − srtt_slow ≥ 50ms` (both relative AND absolute: a 5→11ms LAN blip passes 2× but fails +50ms; a 200→260ms cellular drift passes +50ms but fails 2× — neither alone may trigger). RTT-arm samples are per-rekey (~120s), so its streak requires 2 consecutive *fresh* samples degraded; the honest consequence: RTT-only degradation is detected in minutes, not seconds — loss is the fast arm.
  6. **Trigger (§-open-point re migration↔recovery):** on `Degraded` + dwell elapsed (`QUALITY_RERACE_DWELL_SECS = 300` since `last_quality_rerace_unix`) + FIS-0010 breaker `Closed` (precedence below) → insert into new daemon field `pending_quality_reprobe: BTreeSet<NodeId>` and record the incumbent endpoint as demoted. `sync_traversal_runtime_state` consumes it: `probe_due = existing_logic || pending_quality_reprobe.remove(node)` (per-peer, closing fact 6's gap) and threads `quality_demoted_endpoint: Option<SocketEndpoint>` into the evaluation, which (a) skips the fresh-handshake short-circuit when the current endpoint IS the demoted one (fact 4) and (b) stable-demotes pairs whose remote equals the demoted endpoint to the END of the pair list after the RFC-8445 sort (fact 5's new seam; demote-don't-exclude: if every alternate fails the authenticated handshake, the incumbent still races last and may legitimately win — dwell then blocks re-trigger for 300s). Ordering composition with FIS-0009: priors re-rank first (its Phase 3), incumbent demotion applies last — both stable transforms on the same post-sort seam.
  7. **Failed migration lands in the EXISTING recovery arms with zero new recovery code — step-by-step against real code:** trigger sets the flag → next reconcile (≤1s, :8190) → `sync_traversal_runtime_state` → `traversal_probe_due` true → `evaluate_traversal_probes` (`phase10.rs:5615`, production-called from `daemon.rs:5861`) runs the race (`traversal.rs:1402`; each attempt flips the endpoint via `send_probe` `phase10.rs:102-107` — existing bounded-blip behavior) → outcome hits the verified decision arms (`phase10.rs:5738-5801`): alternate handshake ⇒ `Direct` commit to the alternate (`:5743-5745`); nothing handshakes + relay armed ⇒ `Relay` (`:5758-5760`); no relay ⇒ `FailClosed` arm re-programs the highest-priority direct candidate (`:5778-5790`) — status-quo recovery. All arms run `commit_verified_traversal_path_for_peer` (`:5488-5502`, delegating to `commit_path_change_for_peer` :5457 → `reconfigure_managed_peer` :5474/:5889-5911 → `update_peer_endpoint` :5907) `[verified: sonnet-5]`. The dwell timestamp lives in `PathQualityState` (separate map — survives the fact-8 rebuild).

- **FIS-0010 precedence (interaction matrix, §2 requirement):** quality migration is direct→direct re-selection; the breaker owns direct↔relay damping. Rules: breaker `Open` ⇒ quality trigger suppressed (flag never set); breaker `HalfOpen` ⇒ suppressed (the breaker owns the single trial); breaker `Closed` ⇒ quality trigger allowed, dwell permitting; a quality-triggered race that ends `Relay`/`FailClosed` feeds the breaker's failure-intensity EWMA as one failure indicator (never bypasses it). Anti-oscillation argument: dwell (300s) and breaker cooldown are both pure *suppressors* — each only ever extends quiet periods, neither forces an action — and an action requires ALL gates open simultaneously, so composing them cannot create a cycle either alone permits; disjoint transition classes (direct→direct vs direct↔relay) close the remaining loop. Until FIS-0010 lands, the gate degrades to dwell-only (a `Closed`-constant stub). `[inference]`

- **Honest payoff, 2-3 vs 10-50 peers:** at 2-3 nodes there are typically ≤2 direct candidates per peer; the win is the single scenario FIS-0001 named — a degraded-but-fresh path (laptop on rotten Wi-Fi with a clean LAN candidate idle) that today is locked in until it fully dies — real, occasional. At 10-50 with mobile/cellular members, degraded-but-alive is the common failure texture and the never-re-scored gap bites constantly. Measurement cost is flat either way; the mechanism adds no scale-dependent machinery. `[inference]`

- **Cost / tradeoffs / attack surface:**
  - Wire: **zero** new messages, listeners, responders, or signed fields. The forged-probe-response attack class from FIS-0001's review is *eliminated*, not mitigated (acceptance criteria above).
  - CPU/memory: ~48 B/peer state; one worker command round-trip per Direct peer per second (≤50/s, same channel class as existing `peer_latest_handshake_unix` queries; a batched all-peers request is an internal optimization if measured — trait unchanged). Nothing per-packet, nothing in the 10ms tick (FIS-0012 clean).
  - New failure modes: (1) mistuned thresholds ⇒ race churn — bounded by sustain-streak + dwell + breaker, falsifiers below; (2) a blocked worker stalls the sampling call — same exposure class as the existing per-peer trait queries, no new class; (3) demotion-seam bugs can only reorder the race — a commit still requires an authenticated handshake, so worst case is a slower race, never an unverified path.
  - On-path attacker: can induce loss ⇒ trigger races toward paths they don't control — same power they already have over the current path; off-path: no input surface (criteria #2).

- **Ground-rules check (§1):** WireGuard internals read-only — PASS (consumes `stats()` verbatim; no boringtun change). Primitive-only trait crossing — PASS (`PeerPathSample`: u32/f32/u64; command backends compile unchanged, `Ok(None)` fail-closed default). Fail-closed scoring — PASS (≥2 samples, staleness ⇒ `Insufficient` ⇒ keep path; margin + streak + dwell are structural, not tunable to zero — dwell floor enforced in code, not config). No signed-state round-trip mid-flight — PASS (re-selects only among the already-signed candidate set; identical discretion to the existing race). Shadow-probe nonce/source-binding — superseded structurally (criteria #1/#2; no probe exists to forge). Safe Rust, pump budget untouched — PASS.

- **What would falsify it:** (1) **clean-network flap rate:** >1 quality-triggered race per peer per 24h on an unimpaired lab soak ⇒ the hysteresis is structurally wrong, shelve; target ≈0. (2) **noise floor:** if injected 5% loss / +80ms cannot be detected within 60s without false positives on the clean control, per-rekey RTT granularity is too coarse (echoes FIS-0004's falsifier) ⇒ keep the loss arm only or shelve. (3) if the demoted incumbent wins >~80% of quality-triggered races in live use, alternates were never actually better — the trigger is measuring real degradation but the candidate sets don't contain a remedy; keep the telemetry, drop the trigger. `[inference]`

- **Prior art (post-fix):** Roberts 1959 EWMA control charts (the threshold trigger — the only change-detection citation retained); RFC 6298 SRTT/RTTVAR *smoothing constants only*; QUIC RFC 9000 §9 probe-before-commit as the shape approximated by the race's handshake-gated commit (deviation disclosed: probing flips the live slot); Tailscale magicsock continuous re-evaluation; MPTCP RFC 8684 as the true-MBB contrast this backend's single-endpoint slot cannot offer.

- **Detailed Recommended Patch Implementation Plan:**
  - **New/modified types:** `PeerPathSample` (backend-api, above); `PathQualityTracker`/`PathQualityState`/`PathQualityVerdict {Healthy, Degraded, Insufficient}` (new `rustynetd/src/path_quality.rs`); daemon fields `path_quality: PathQualityTracker`, `pending_quality_reprobe: BTreeSet<NodeId>`; `RuntimeRequest::PeerPathSample` variant in both `userspace_shared/runtime.rs` and `userspace_shared_macos/runtime.rs`; engine accessor `peer_path_sample` (lands once, shared engine.rs).
  - **Signatures:** trait method above (default `Ok(None)`, object-safe — fact 10); `evaluate_traversal_probes` gains `quality_demoted_endpoint: Option<SocketEndpoint>` (default `None` = byte-identical); a pair-list post-sort demotion helper in `ice_priority.rs` (`demote_pairs_matching(pairs: &mut Vec<CandidatePair>, endpoint: SocketAddr)`, stable).
  - **Call sites (verified):** `daemon.rs` `reconcile()` :8190 vicinity (sampling + verdict + trigger); `sync_traversal_runtime_state` :5613/:5768 (per-peer flag consumption); `daemon.rs:5861` → `phase10.rs:5615` (threading the demotion param); status/netcheck lines :5541/:7147-7148 gain `path_quality_srtt_ms= path_quality_loss= path_quality_verdict= path_quality_reraces=` (safe per fact 9).
  - **Decision sketch:** `verdict(state) == Degraded && now − last_quality_rerace ≥ 300 && breaker == Closed → { pending_quality_reprobe.insert(node); demoted = current_endpoint; last_quality_rerace = now }`; race side: `if Some(cur) == demoted { skip fresh-handshake short-circuit }; pairs = rfc8445_sort(...); fis0009_rerank_if_enabled(...); demote_pairs_matching(&mut pairs, demoted)`.
  - **Existing tests that must keep passing (named, `[verified: sonnet-5]`):** phase10 — `traversal_probe_uses_existing_fresh_handshake_on_current_endpoint` :10545, `traversal_probe_promotes_direct_when_handshake_advances` :10613, `traversal_probe_falls_back_to_relay_when_handshake_does_not_advance` :10689, `traversal_probe_keeps_signed_direct_programmed_when_handshake_does_not_advance_and_no_relay_exists` :10765, `traversal_probe_declines_direct_without_valid_coordination_when_relay_is_armed` :10841, `traversal_probe_fails_closed_without_valid_coordination_and_without_relay` :10917, `test_commit_path_change_is_the_only_apply_path` :12335 (all take `quality_demoted_endpoint = None` ⇒ unchanged); daemon — :22318 `…periodic_reprobe_recovers_direct_after_relay`, :22486 `…direct_health_uses_live_handshake_without_forced_reprobe`, :22642 `…direct_liveness_expiry_falls_back_to_relay`, :22795 `…recovers_direct_when_handshake_arrives`, :20457 format test (substring asserts unaffected); backend — `contract_stats_peer_count_reflects_configured_peers` (`backend_contract.rs:484`, `stub_conformance.rs:294`), `linux_userspace_shared_backend_authenticated_engine_activity_updates_handshake_and_stats` (`userspace_shared/mod.rs:2426`), `macos_userspace_shared_backend_configures_peer_and_stats` (`userspace_shared_macos/mod.rs:2483`), `linux_backend_reads_latest_handshake_for_configured_peer` (`linux_command.rs:939`), `latest_handshake_parser_rejects_oversized_or_malformed_output` (:968), `windows_backend_stats_and_handshakes_are_read_from_wg_show` (`windows_command.rs:1261`).
  - **New tests:** path_quality module — `path_quality_insufficient_until_two_rtt_samples`, `path_quality_stale_samples_yield_insufficient`, `path_quality_rtt_ingest_requires_handshake_advance`, `path_quality_loss_streak_triggers_degraded`, `path_quality_rtt_needs_relative_and_absolute_margin`, `path_quality_dwell_blocks_repeat_trigger`; backend — `contract_peer_path_sample_defaults_to_none` (contract suite ⇒ stub + command backends), `linux_userspace_shared_peer_path_sample_returns_live_loss_and_rtt`, macOS mirror; phase10 — `traversal_probe_quality_demotion_skips_fresh_handshake_short_circuit`, `traversal_probe_quality_demoted_incumbent_races_last_and_can_still_win`, `traversal_probe_quality_race_failure_lands_in_existing_relay_arm`; daemon — `quality_rerace_shadow_mode_logs_without_action`, `quality_rerace_respects_dwell_and_breaker_gate`, `quality_rerace_flag_off_is_byte_identical`.
  - **Live-lab stage:** `validate_quality_triggered_rerace` — dual-candidate Linux topology (clean + impairable path to the same peer), tc-netem 8% loss + 80ms on the active candidate; PASS = verdict flips `Degraded` and the forced race commits the clean candidate within lab-dwell(30s)+race budget with handshake gap ≤ 30s, run-matrix row appended; companion clean-soak stage asserts zero quality races in 2h (falsifier 1's short form).
  - **Commit sequence + effort:** 1 (S) `path_quality.rs` pure module + full unit suite, unwired; 2 (S) backend-api `PeerPathSample` + trait default + userspace_shared plumbing (engine accessor, request variant, worker arm) + contract tests; 3 (S) macOS runtime mirror; 4 (M) daemon shadow mode — sampling loop, tracker, verdicts, status fields, "would-force-rerace" structured log, NO behavior change; 5 (M) gated action — pending set, per-peer probe_due arm, demotion seam (evaluate_traversal_probes param + `demote_pairs_matching` + short-circuit skip), breaker-precedence stub, config flag `path_quality_rerace_enabled` default OFF + tests; 6 (M lab / L decision) live-lab stage + clean-soak evidence, then and only then the default flip.

## Focused pass — Considered and rejected (path quality / FIS-0001 revision)

- **STUN-style shadow probe to the peer's WG port (FIS-0001's original mechanism)** — killed on three verified facts: no responder can exist (unmatched-source datagrams are dropped pre-crypto, `engine.rs:268-270`/`:372-377` `[verified: sonnet-5]`); adding one means an **unauthenticated responder on the WireGuard port**, destroying WG's deliberate silence-to-unauthenticated-probes property (fingerprinting + reflection surface) — disqualifying in this repo's security posture; and the existing round-trip primitive is a source-address-matched singleton whose `reject_round_trip_target` explicitly refuses configured-peer endpoints (`runtime.rs:772-780` `[verified: first-hand read]`) — the transport was deliberately shaped never to do request/response with peers.
- **Rustynet echo on the gossip port** — gossip has zero production attachment (`attach_gossip_runtime`, zero callers, verified in FIS-0003), so this gates path quality on an unshipped subsystem, and the unauthenticated-responder objection applies on any port.
- **WG-handshake-initiation-as-probe to the alternate address without reconfiguring** — structurally impossible today: the response would arrive from an address that matches no configured peer endpoint and is dropped before decapsulation (`engine.rs:372-377`, `supports_roaming: false` `[verified: sonnet-5]`); making it routable means receiver-index routing / roaming — engine surgery out of scope, and it would entangle probing with live-session rekey state.
- **True make-before-break (second live conversation per peer)** — requires a multi-endpoint trait + multi-session engine; FIS-0001 already disclosed the single-slot limit as its weakest point; MPTCP-class work, out of scope.
- **Engine-side EWMA home (FIS-0004's original in-engine `BTreeMap`)** — rejected for the shared layer: policy-adjacent state below the trait boundary, pump-adjacent update work (FIS-0012 territory), and the daemon must re-aggregate for dwell/breaker composition anyway; the raw-sample-up / smooth-in-daemon split mirrors the `peer_latest_handshake_unix` precedent exactly. FIS-0004's pacing gate consumes a daemon-pushed hint instead.
- **Real CUSUM** — at ≤1 RTT sample per ~120s rekey, a cumulative log-likelihood statistic has no detection-power advantage over sustain-counters; implementing it would be citation-driven complexity (review fix #1 applied by deletion). `[inference]`

## Focused pass — Coverage note (path quality / FIS-0001 revision)

- The macOS runtime's request-enum internals were not re-read this pass (mirror commit sized from FIS-0012's verified precedent that the two runtime files are twins; engine.rs confirmed shared).
- Relay-path quality (`PathMode::Relay` peers) is deliberately out of scope — sampling covers Direct peers only; relay fleet quality belongs to FIS-0007's territory.
- The batched all-peers sampling request is noted but not designed; the dual-candidate live-lab netns topology is assumed available from the cross-network substrate work (X1) — unverified.
- FIS-0010's `TraversalProbeStatus` field-carryover wrinkle (fact 8) is flagged as a coordination note, not resolved here.
- **Method:** self-authored; four narrow Sonnet 5 read-only checks ran (phase10 probe/commit shapes + race internals; daemon probe pass/force_reprobe/status-format tests; engine inbound routing/roaming + trait-impl mechanics; dyn usage + command backends + test census — the last retried once after a transient failure). Several checks **changed the design**: no-roaming + pre-crypto source-address drop killed the handshake-as-probe variant and the roaming-self-heal assumption; the fresh-handshake short-circuit (phase10.rs:10545) forced the explicit skip in the demotion seam; `force_reprobe`-is-global forced the per-peer pending set; the `TraversalProbeStatus` full-rebuild (daemon.rs:5911) forced the separate tracker map; and the engine.rs:531 "test helper" claim in FIS-0001/0004 was found false (it is `authenticated_handshake_unix` on the per-packet drive paths) and corrected above. Line numbers verified 2026-07-02; they will drift.

# Focused pass — adaptive keepalive-interval estimation — 2026-07-02

> Grounding note: this pass was read and verified against a fresh `origin/main` (`5868a09`, default branch confirmed `main`) in a disposable worktree (`.claude/worktrees/fable-keepalive`, removed after the pass), not the primary checkout. The worktree's copy of this doc tops out at FIS-0012; FIS-0013/0014 exist uncommitted in the primary checkout, so this entry takes **FIS-0015** and is appended to the primary's copy (the worktree copy is destroyed on cleanup).

## FIS-0015: Censored-gap keepalive-lifetime search — per-mapping AIMD interval estimation with NAT-class-gated raising

- **Pipeline / area:** keepalive scheduling — `crates/rustynetd/src/relay_client.rs` + its daemon call site (the one LIVE keepalive path), `crates/rustynetd/src/traversal.rs` (the orphaned NAT-aware logic), `rustynet-backend-api`/`rustynet-backend-wireguard` (the never-wired WireGuard-native site). Pure timing: nothing here changes packet contents, eligibility, or any authenticated surface.

- **Grounded problem statement — the three-sites picture, corrected by verification:**
  1. **Site 1 (traversal.rs) — dead, and deader than assumed.** `TraversalSession::recommended_keepalive_secs` (`traversal.rs:1081-1087`: 15s if `is_hard_nat() || !preserves_port`, else 25s) has zero production callers; its only exerciser is `keepalive_interval_is_tighter_for_hard_nat` (`traversal.rs:1984-1999`). `should_send_keepalive` (`:1089`) and `mark_keepalive_sent` (`:1097`) have **zero references beyond their definitions — not even tests**. All three sit on `TraversalSession`, which is never instantiated outside `#[cfg(test)]` `[verified: sonnet-5]`.
  2. **Site 2 (relay client) — live, flat 25s.** Production constructs `RelayClientConfig` exactly twice, both `::default()` (25s): `daemon.rs:3686` and `:3715` inside `load_relay_client()`. Consumption: `sessions_needing_keepalive` (`relay_client.rs:666-673`) filters sessions on `last_activity.elapsed() >= keepalive_interval`; its sole production caller is `daemon.rs:5634` inside `sync_traversal_runtime_state` (driven from the ~1s reconcile tick via `:4579`), which sends the 5-byte relay keepalive (`send_keepalive_with_sender`, `relay_client.rs:694-719`) over the authoritative transport. No production code ever sets a non-default interval; the `keepalive_interval()` accessor (`:658`) has no production caller `[verified: sonnet-5]`.
  3. **Site 3 (WireGuard-native `PersistentKeepalive`) — never configured, anywhere, and the engine couldn't fire it anyway.** The only production `Tunn::new` call (`engine.rs:155-162`) passes `None` in the `persistent_keepalive` position (param 4 of 6, `boringtun/src/noise/mod.rs:193-201`); `PeerConfig` (`backend-api/src/lib.rs:71-77`) has no keepalive field; the three command backends' `wg set` peer paths (linux `:351-381`, macos `:467-483`, windows `:332-348` + conf-writer `:258-298`) never pass `persistent-keepalive`. Every remaining mention is two e2e helper bins (hardcoding `persistent-keepalive 5`), one diagnostic config-stanza generator (`"PersistentKeepalive = 25"`), and two doc comments in `port_mapper.rs` (:2129, :2182). Sharper still: the engine never drives boringtun's timer machinery at all (`update_timers`/`timer_tick`: zero call sites — also independently recorded in `SecurityAndQualityAudit_2026-06-10.md`), so even passing `Some(n)` to `Tunn::new` would send nothing `[verified: sonnet-5]`.
  4. **The cold-start prior has no live input today:** `NatProfile` (`traversal.rs:903`) is constructed only in test fixtures, derives no `Serialize`, and no function returns one; the real classifier (`classify_nat` → `NatClassHeuristic`, `ops_cross_network_preflight.rs:127/:355`, multi-STUN XOR-MAPPED-ADDRESS comparison on one shared socket, classifying the *local* NAT) is a standalone CLI diagnostic that `rustynetd` never reads `[verified: sonnet-5]` (consistent with FIS-0009's findings).
  Net: today the mesh sends **one kind** of keepalive (relay sessions, flat 25s for every peer and every router) and **no keepalive at all** on direct WireGuard paths — an idle direct tunnel's NAT mapping dies silently and is resurrected by a re-race on next use. A router that expires UDP mappings in <25s (real consumer firmware does — RFC 4787 REQ-5 mandates ≥2min but compliance is notoriously inconsistent `[inference]`) defeats the relay keepalive every cycle, currently masked by the re-establish-once machinery (pinned by `daemon_runtime_relay_keepalive_failure_reestablishes_once_on_authoritative_transport`, `daemon.rs:21537`).

- **Named mechanism: per-mapping censored-gap AIMD search (PLPMTUD-shaped), NAT-class-gated raising.**
  The binding timeout T of a NAT mapping is not directly observable — only *censored* binary evidence exists: a gap of G seconds followed by inbound evidence ⇒ T > G (survival); a gap of G followed by attributable loss ⇒ T ≤ G (failure). That observation model is RFC 4821 PLPMTUD's, not RTO estimation's — so the estimator is a bounded probe-search with a confirmed-safe watermark, **not** a mean+variance EWMA. Jacobson/Karels is borrowed only for its discipline (maintain a running estimate, operate at estimate-minus-safety-margin, update on every observation) — explicitly NOT its SRTT/RTTVAR form, because censored binaries carry no variance signal to smooth `[inference]`. Granularity note: a NAT mapping is keyed per (internal socket, remote endpoint) — on address/port-dependent NATs each peer/relay has its OWN mapping with its own timeout — so per-peer estimators (keyed `NodeId`/relay id) are the *correct* granularity, not merely a convenience `[inference]`.

  ```rust
  // new module: crates/rustynetd/src/keepalive.rs — pure, no clocks, no I/O
  pub const KEEPALIVE_FLOOR_SECS: u16 = 10;    // relay test already pins default >= 10s
  pub const KEEPALIVE_CEILING_SECS: u16 = 50;  // see safety argument
  pub const KEEPALIVE_RAISE_STEP_SECS: u16 = 5;
  pub const KEEPALIVE_RAISE_AFTER_SURVIVALS: u8 = 8;

  #[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
  pub enum KeepalivePrior { RelaySession, DirectEasyNat, DirectHardOrUnknownNat }
  // prior_interval_secs: RelaySession => 25 (grandfathered production value),
  //   DirectEasyNat => 25, DirectHardOrUnknownNat => 15  (site-1 values, resurrected as the prior)

  #[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]
  pub struct KeepaliveEstimator {
      operating_secs: u16,        // the interval actually used
      confirmed_safe_secs: u16,   // longest gap with positive survival evidence
      failed_low_secs: u16,       // shortest gap with attributed loss (0 = none seen)
      survivals_at_operating: u8, // consecutive survivals since last change
      raise_enabled: bool,        // NAT-class gate: false for DirectHardOrUnknownNat
  }
  ```
  Update rule (pure fns, one branch each):
  - `on_survival(gap)`: `confirmed_safe = max(confirmed_safe, gap)`; `survivals += 1` (saturating).
  - `on_binding_loss(gap)`: `failed_low = if failed_low == 0 { gap } else { min(failed_low, gap) }`; `operating = max(FLOOR, min(operating, confirmed_safe))`; if the loss occurred at `gap <= operating` (the base interval itself failed, not a probe) additionally `operating = max(FLOOR, operating - STEP)`; `survivals = 0`. Decreases are immediate and unconditional.
  - `next_gap()`: if `raise_enabled && survivals >= RAISE_AFTER && operating + STEP <= CEILING && (failed_low == 0 || operating + 2*STEP <= failed_low)` → return `operating + STEP` as a **single probe cycle** (on survival: `operating += STEP`, `survivals = 0`; on loss: clamp per above). Else return `operating`. Raises are additive, single-step, evidence-gated, class-gated, and never approach a recorded failure closer than one step.
  - Cold start: `operating = prior`, everything else zero/empty — behavior identical to the static value until evidence accumulates, i.e. cold start degrades to exactly the already-proven defaults (25s relay = today's production value; 15/25 direct = site 1's tested values with **unknown NAT ⇒ 15s**, since no live `NatProfile` exists — fact 4).

  **Why the class gate (the design's load-bearing asymmetry):** what a mapping expiry *costs* differs by NAT class. On an endpoint-independent, port-preserving NAT, our next outbound packet transparently re-creates the mapping (usually same public port) — an overlong probe costs a bounded inbound-blackout window of ≤ one cycle, self-healing. On a symmetric/non-preserving NAT, rebirth lands on a NEW public port — the peer's signed view of our endpoint breaks and a full re-coordination is needed. So upward probing is enabled exactly where expiry is self-healing (`DirectEasyNat`; `RelaySession`, where the daemon's re-establish-once path — `daemon.rs:21537` test — is the proven safety net) and disabled where it isn't (`DirectHardOrUnknownNat` stays pinned at 15s, learning only DOWNWARD on observed failure). This is the §2 asymmetry made structural: under-sending is one 5-byte packet; over-stretching is only ever risked where recovery is automatic. `[inference]`

- **Observation sources (what actually feeds `on_survival`/`on_binding_loss`):**
  - **Relay sessions (live today):** the gap is `last_activity.elapsed()` at keepalive-send time (already computed at `relay_client.rs:670`); survival = the session continuing without re-establishment through the next cycle; loss = the existing keepalive-failure→re-establish event (`daemon.rs:5634` error arm / `:21537` behavior). Attribution is noisy (a relay restart also triggers it) — mis-attribution only ever *tightens* the interval, the cheap direction, so noisy attribution is acceptable by construction.
  - **Direct peers (after wiring):** survival = inbound evidence after a gap — `latest_handshake_unix` advance (`traversal_handshake_is_fresh` chain, `daemon.rs:5818-5826` → `phase10.rs:5604-5613`, real and per-peer today `[verified: sonnet-5]`) or per-peer `rx_bytes` advance once FIS-0013's `PeerPathSample` lands (per-peer rx is NOT reachable from the daemon today — aggregate-only `TunnelStats`, linux/macos command backends hardcode 0, windows sums per-peer rows away `[verified: sonnet-5]`). WireGuard's passive-keepalive rule makes our keepalive elicit a peer keepalive within ~10s, so each cycle yields a usable binary observation when the tunnel is otherwise idle `[inference]`. Loss = handshake-freshness expiry / re-race on the same incumbent endpoint (FIS-0013's signals). No-evidence cycles (peer fully idle, nothing inbound) count as NEITHER — raising is evidence-gated, so an idle peer's estimator simply freezes at its last confirmed value.

- **How it plugs into the three sites (one shared estimator, three consumers):**
  - Daemon owns `keepalive_estimators: BTreeMap<NodeId, KeepaliveEstimator>` (relay ids and direct peers share the map — distinct keys).
  - **Site 2 (first live wiring):** add `sessions_with_elapsed(&self) -> Vec<(NodeId, Duration)>` beside `sessions_needing_keepalive` in `relay_client.rs`; the `daemon.rs:5634` loop filters by the per-peer `estimator.next_gap()` instead of the flat config threshold, records survival/loss per cycle, and leaves `RelayClientConfig::keepalive_interval` in place as the documented prior/fallback (existing fn + tests untouched).
  - **Site 3, command backends:** add `persistent_keepalive_secs: Option<u16>` to `PeerConfig`; linux/macos/windows command backends append `persistent-keepalive <n>` to their existing `wg set` arg builders (+ the windows conf stanza); value = the estimator's operating interval at (re)configure time — coarse adaptivity, updated on the existing reconfigure path only. Native `wg` then does the sending.
  - **Site 3, userspace-shared:** boringtun's timers are not driven (fact 3), so do NOT route through `Tunn`'s `persistent_keepalive`. Instead: new trait method `fn send_peer_keepalive(&mut self, _node_id: &NodeId) -> Result<(), BackendError> { Ok(()) }` (default no-op — the `initiate_peer_handshake` precedent; dyn-compatible, command backends unaffected since native wg covers them); userspace impl encapsulates a zero-length plaintext (the canonical WG keepalive packet) on the peer's `Tunn` and sends via the authoritative socket — a worker request mirroring the existing per-peer command pattern, mirrored into `userspace_shared_macos` as usual. The daemon's reconcile tick consults the estimator per Direct peer and fires it — scheduling stays daemon-side, identically across platforms; only the send primitive differs per backend family (stated per §2: relay-client keepalive is shared code; WG-native is per-backend).
  - **Site 1 disposition (§3d):** **subsumed, not resurrected.** The 15/25 logic moves into `KeepalivePrior` (the cold-start prior — reuse justified: they're the only NAT-conditioned, unit-tested timing values in the tree); `recommended_keepalive_secs` becomes a thin delegate so `keepalive_interval_is_tighter_for_hard_nat` keeps passing until `TraversalSession`'s fate is settled by FIS-0010; `should_send_keepalive`/`mark_keepalive_sent` are deleted outright — zero references, zero tests, and the estimator's `next_gap`/`on_*` API replaces their exact roles `[verified: sonnet-5 — deletion is free]`.

- **Why it's actually better:** today's flat 25s relay keepalive silently loses to any <25s-timeout router (each cycle: dead mapping → failed keepalive → re-establish round-trip — permanent churn, currently invisible); the adaptive version converges to timeout−margin and stops the churn. Direct paths today have NO keepalive: idle tunnels die and pay a re-race on next use; wiring the estimator gives always-warm paths at 2-6 packets/min, and the adaptive raise halves that on generous routers (25s→50s = 50% fewer radio wake-ups — the mobile/battery case). Honestly: at 2-3 peers the estimator itself is the smaller half of the win — the *wiring* (any direct-path keepalive at all; per-peer relay intervals) is the bigger half, and the estimator is what makes the wiring safe to run against hostile-router diversity without hand-tuning. `[inference]`

- **Safety argument (§2 walkthrough):** FLOOR = 10s (the existing `relay_client_config_has_reasonable_defaults` test already asserts the default ≥ 10s — the floor is compatible by construction; below 10s is radio-wakeup abuse with no NAT that needs it `[inference]`). CEILING = 50s absolute, unconditional, enforced in `next_gap` regardless of history: 2× the WG-convention 25s, and 2.4× under RFC 4787's 120s compliant minimum — a spec-compliant router is never at risk even at ceiling; only non-compliant routers can fail there, and those are exactly the ones the estimator observes and clamps on. Raising: additive (+5s), one probe cycle at a time, only after 8 consecutive confirmed survivals, only in self-healing NAT classes, never within one step of a recorded failure. Falling: immediate, unconditional, monotone toward FLOOR. Unknown NAT = hard prior, no raising. No evidence = no raising. Every uncertain state resolves to "send more often," never "send less often" — the one-sided margin is structural because the cost function is one-sided (a wasted keepalive is 5-32 bytes; a lost mapping is a reconnect). `[inference]`

- **Cost / tradeoffs:** 16 bytes + one map entry per peer; O(1) integer arithmetic per keepalive cycle (~1/25s/peer — thousands of times below any budget that matters); zero wire-format changes (packets unchanged — pure timing). Code complexity is the honest cost: three currently-trivial call sites gain an estimator consultation, and site 3's userspace lane adds a new trait method + worker request + macOS mirror. New failure modes: (1) mis-attributed losses (peer offline ≠ NAT expiry) over-tighten toward FLOOR — bounded, cheap direction, self-corrects as survivals re-accumulate; (2) a probe-raise failure on `DirectEasyNat` costs one bounded inbound-blackout cycle (self-healing rebirth); (3) estimator state is in-memory only — a daemon restart re-runs cold start from the prior (deliberate: persisting learned timeouts is a FIS-0009-style prior-store extension, out of scope). At 2-3 peers the state cost is nil; the complexity is justified by the correctness fix (hostile routers) more than the efficiency win. `[inference]`

- **What would falsify it:** in the live-lab NAT substrate with the netns UDP conntrack timeout set per-profile to {12s, 30s, 90s}: (1) at 12s, static-25s relay keepalive must show measurable re-establish churn AND the adaptive version must converge to ≤ 12s−margin within ~10 cycles and hold zero churn thereafter — if it doesn't, the loss-attribution signal is too weak, shelve; (2) at 90s, the adaptive version must reach ≥ 40s operating (≥ 40% fewer keepalives than static) — if raising never engages, the survival-evidence plumbing isn't earning its complexity, ship wiring + static priors only; (3) on a clean 90s profile the interval must never exceed 50s and never oscillate (>1 raise-clamp cycle per hour = hysteresis failure). `[inference]`

- **Prior art:** RFC 4821 (PLPMTUD) — probing a hidden path property with confirmed-safe state, bounded search range, probe-failure clamping: the actual mechanism shape. Jacobson & Karels 1988 / RFC 6298 — the estimate-plus-margin operating discipline ONLY (explicitly not the mean+variance form: censored binary observations carry no variance to smooth — this is the "using it correctly" statement). RFC 4787 REQ-5 (≥2min compliant UDP mapping timeout) for the ceiling argument; RFC 8445 §11 (ICE 15s-default keepalives) and WireGuard's 25s persistent-keepalive convention for the priors; Chiu-Jain AIMD for the additive-raise/immediate-clamp asymmetry; home-gateway timeout-diversity measurement literature (e.g. Hätönen et al. 2010) for router-diversity motivation `[inference — literature not re-fetched this pass]`.

- **Detailed Recommended Patch Implementation Plan:**
  - **New:** `crates/rustynetd/src/keepalive.rs` — `KeepalivePrior`, `KeepaliveEstimator` (fields/constants above), pure API `new(prior)`, `on_survival(gap_secs: u16)`, `on_binding_loss(gap_secs: u16)`, `next_gap(&self) -> u16`, `operating_secs(&self) -> u16`. Daemon field `keepalive_estimators: BTreeMap<NodeId, KeepaliveEstimator>`.
  - **Modified:** `relay_client.rs` — add `pub fn sessions_with_elapsed(&self) -> Vec<(NodeId, Duration)>` (keep `sessions_needing_keepalive` intact for compat + its tests); `daemon.rs:5634` loop — per-peer threshold from the estimator + survival/loss recording; `backend-api/src/lib.rs` — `PeerConfig.persistent_keepalive_secs: Option<u16>` + `fn send_peer_keepalive(...) -> Result<(), BackendError> { Ok(()) }` default; command backends — append `persistent-keepalive` to the `wg set` arg builders (linux `:351-381`, macos `:467-483`, windows `:332-348` + conf stanza `:258-298`); userspace_shared + macos mirror — `RuntimeRequest::SendPeerKeepalive` + engine zero-length-encapsulate send; traversal.rs — `recommended_keepalive_secs` delegates to `KeepalivePrior`, delete `should_send_keepalive`/`mark_keepalive_sent`.
  - **Pseudocode (per relay/direct keepalive cycle):** `gap = elapsed_since_last_activity(peer); if gap >= est.next_gap() { record survival(prev_gap) if inbound evidence since last send else neither; send keepalive; } on re-establish/stale event: est.on_binding_loss(observed_gap)`.
  - **Existing tests that must keep passing (named, `[verified: sonnet-5]`):** `keepalive_interval_is_tighter_for_hard_nat` (traversal.rs:1984 — kept via the delegate; extended in commit 1 with the `None`⇒15 unknown-NAT case); `relay_client_config_has_reasonable_defaults` (:1043), `relay_client_sessions_needing_keepalive_returns_stale_sessions` (:1941), `relay_client_keepalive_interval_returns_config_value` (:2047), `relay_client_send_keepalive_with_sender_uses_allocated_port` (:2193), `relay_client_send_keepalive_without_authoritative_transport_fails_closed` (:2344); daemon relay-keepalive trio `daemon_runtime_relay_establish_and_keepalive_use_backend_shared_transport_identity` (:21446), `…_keepalive_failure_reestablishes_once_…` (:21537), `…_keepalive_reestablish_failure_fail_closes` (:21627); port-mapper mode tests (`port_mapping_mode_default_is_keepalive` :4144 et al. — untouched, different subsystem); `test_keepalive_rejects_unbound_and_wrong_tuple_activity` (rustynet-relay transport.rs:2026 — untouched).
  - **New tests:** `keepalive_estimator_cold_start_matches_static_priors` (all three priors); `keepalive_estimator_unknown_nat_defaults_hard_15s`; `keepalive_estimator_tightens_immediately_on_loss`; `keepalive_estimator_never_exceeds_ceiling_regardless_of_history` (property-style: arbitrary observation sequences, assert `next_gap() <= 50` always); `keepalive_estimator_raise_gated_on_nat_class_and_survival_count`; `keepalive_estimator_never_raises_within_step_of_recorded_failure`; `keepalive_estimator_two_peers_converge_independently` (12s-router peer → 10s floor; 90s-router peer → ceiling-bounded raise); `relay_keepalive_uses_per_peer_estimator_interval` (daemon); `send_peer_keepalive_emits_zero_length_wireguard_packet` (+ macOS mirror); `command_backend_wg_set_includes_persistent_keepalive_when_configured` (per backend).
  - **Commit sequence + effort:** 1 (S) `keepalive.rs` pure estimator + full unit/property suite + `KeepalivePrior` subsuming site 1's values (traversal delegate + deletions), unwired; 2 (M) site 2 wiring — `sessions_with_elapsed`, per-peer thresholds + observation recording at `daemon.rs:5634`, telemetry fields in status line, shadow log of would-be intervals first; 3 (S) `PeerConfig.persistent_keepalive_secs` + command-backend `wg set`/conf plumbing (static value from prior; estimator-driven on reconfigure); 4 (M-L, needs design sign-off — new behavior: keepalives where none existed) userspace-shared `send_peer_keepalive` + macOS mirror + daemon direct-peer scheduling gated behind a default-off config flag; 5 (M lab) live-lab stage `validate_adaptive_keepalive_convergence` (nft conntrack-timeout profiles {12,30,90}s + the falsifier assertions) → default-on decision.

## Focused pass — Considered and rejected (adaptive keepalive)

- **Jacobson/Karels mean+variance EWMA over "observed timeouts"** — the timeout is never directly observed (only censored above/below bounds), so an EWMA of gaps measures our own sending schedule, not the router; it can never learn the timeout is LONGER than what we allow (self-censoring) and its variance term is meaningless on binary evidence. Kept only as the margin discipline; the mechanism is a bounded search. `[inference]`
- **Symmetric probing on all NAT classes** — a probe-raise past the true timeout on a symmetric/non-preserving NAT costs a public-port change and full re-coordination, violating §2's "err short under uncertainty"; raising is therefore class-gated off for hard/unknown NATs rather than margin-tuned. `[inference]`
- **Routing WG-native keepalive through `Tunn::new(persistent_keepalive=Some(n))` for the userspace backend** — dead on arrival: the engine never calls boringtun's `update_timers`/`timer_tick` (zero call sites `[verified: sonnet-5]`), so the timer would never fire; driving the full boringtun timer machinery just for keepalives is far more invasive than one zero-length-encapsulate send on the daemon's existing tick.
- **Resurrecting `TraversalSession` to host the estimator** — the type has zero production callers and FIS-0010 already treats its counter FSM as a vestigial baseline; bolting new live state onto a dead type inverts the dependency. The 15/25 values are extracted; the husk is left to FIS-0010's disposition. `[verified: sonnet-5]` (deadness) / `[inference]` (disposition).
- **Persisting learned timeouts across restarts** — attractive (FIS-0009's prior-store shape) but out of scope: cold start already degrades to proven values, and persisted-but-stale timeout state is a fresh way to be wrong after a router swap; revisit alongside FIS-0009's `PeerTraversalPrior` store if that lands. `[inference]`

## Focused pass — Coverage note (adaptive keepalive)

- **Verifier substitution, disclosed:** the tasked `opencode run -m opencode/deepseek-v4-flash-free` route could not run in this session's sandboxed shell (global npm install blocked; local install succeeded but every invocation hung with zero output and exit 124), and the repo's `rustynet-deepseek` MCP fallback reported no API key configured. Per the repo's own "if the server is down, proceed without it" rule, the five §4 checks (a-e) ran instead as independent read-only **Sonnet 5** agents against the fresh worktree — same independence intent, different verifier — hence `[verified: sonnet-5]` tags throughout rather than `[verified: deepseek-flash]`. All five checks confirmed the claims under test; refinements they added: `should_send_keepalive`/`mark_keepalive_sent` are wholly unreferenced (stronger than "test-only"); the e2e bins use `persistent-keepalive 5` (not 25); boringtun's timer machinery is entirely undriven by the engine; `relay_client_config_has_reasonable_defaults` already pins ≥10s (making the FLOOR compatible by construction); and the relay keepalive failure→re-establish path is already tested, giving the raise-gate its safety net for `RelaySession`.
- WireGuard's passive-keepalive echo (our keepalive eliciting the peer's within ~10s) is asserted from protocol knowledge, not re-verified against boringtun's timers.rs this pass — flagged `[inference]`; commit 4's design sign-off should confirm it before relying on it as the idle-tunnel survival signal.
- The windows command backend's conf-file-vs-`wg set` dual path was located but the estimator-update-on-reconfigure frequency for it was not analyzed; nor was per-relay (vs per-peer) estimator keying for multi-relay fleets (FIS-0007 territory).
- Battery/radio quantification is directional, not measured; the live-lab NAT-timeout substrate knob (netns conntrack timeout) is assumed available from the X1 NAT-matrix work — unverified.
- Worktree used: `origin/main` @ `5868a09`; removed after the pass. Line numbers verified 2026-07-02 against that commit; they will drift.

# Focused pass — retry/backoff consolidation + jitter — 2026-07-02

> Grounding note: read and verified against fresh `origin/main` (`5868a09`, default branch confirmed `main`) in a disposable worktree (`.claude/worktrees/fable-backoff`, removed after the pass). Worktree doc numbering tops at FIS-0012; FIS-0013/0014/0015 exist uncommitted in the primary checkout, so this entry takes **FIS-0016**.

## FIS-0016: Full-Jitter completion of the orphaned backoff primitive + a classified no-migration verdict for every hand-rolled retry site

- **Pipeline / area:** `crates/rustynetd/src/resilience.rs` (the primitive) + a repo-wide retry/poll census. Pure timing/scheduling; no packet contents, no trust surface.

- **Grounded problem statement (corrected against verification):**
  - `ReconnectPolicy { initial_backoff_ms: 250, multiplier: 2, max_backoff_ms: 5_000 }` and the pure `next_reconnect_delay_ms(policy, attempt)` = `min(cap, initial · multiplier^attempt)` (saturating) live at `resilience.rs:18-33/:62-66`, pinned by `reconnect_policy_exponential_backoff_is_capped` (`:392-402`, exact values 200/400/800/1000). **Zero callers exist anywhere in the workspace** — no production file, test, bin, or fuzz target references either symbol; `daemon.rs`'s import of `crate::resilience` (`:56-58`) conspicuously pulls only the session-snapshot items. The module itself is live (snapshot persistence used at `daemon.rs:8023/:8029/:8084/:8089` + three mesh-status collectors); the backoff corner is dead code inside a live module `[verified: fact-check]`.
  - **The §0.2 "three retry structs" claim needed two corrections:** the NAT-PMP (`round_trip`, `port_mapper.rs:428-455`, 250ms/9 attempts per RFC 6886 §3.1) and PCP (`:860-886`, 250ms/5 attempts — a *documented deviation* from RFC 6887 §8.1.1's IRT=3s/MRC=0, with an operator override and rationale comments at `:620-639`) loops are real; but both double the **socket read timeout** (`current_timeout.saturating_mul(2)` at `:447`/`:879`) with the retransmit firing immediately after each timeout — **no inter-attempt sleep exists**. They are receive-timeout retransmission ladders, not delay-before-retry backoff — the same arithmetic as `next_reconnect_delay_ms` but different semantics. The third struct (`PortMappingProbe`, `:2404+`) has **no retry loop at all** — it plumbs `initial_timeout`/`max_attempts` into the two clients (`:2485-2487`, `:2500-2502`) and does a single PCP→NAT-PMP→uPnP fallthrough `[verified: fact-check]`.
  - **§0.4 correction:** `privileged_helper.rs:3509` is not a retry site — it is a `#[cfg(test)]` loop iterating shell-injection *payload strings* named `injection_attempts` (`:3502-3516`) `[verified: fact-check]`.
  - **No recorded rationale for the divergence:** resilience.rs predates all the hand-rolled loops by 7-12 weeks (`479d6ef` 2026-02-27 vs. port_mapper `e0e9a96` 2026-05-18, windows_runtime_boundary `4e6feb0`/file 2026-04-18, killswitch-precedence `3c71724`/file 2026-05-23); zero cross-references in comments, commit messages, or `documents/` — parallel evolution, not deliberate choice `[verified: fact-check]`.
  - **A second copy of the identical formula already exists:** `rustynet-control/src/lib.rs:489-503` `register_failure` computes `initial_backoff_secs · 2^exponent` capped at `max_backoff_secs` for an enrollment/auth lockout — the duplicate-formula drift the orphaned primitive was presumably meant to prevent has already happened once `[verified: fact-check]`.

- **The jitter design (§1b):** **AWS Full Jitter** (Brooker, "Exponential Backoff and Jitter," AWS Architecture Blog 2015): `delay = uniform_random(0, min(cap, base · multiplier^attempt))` — represented exactly, with the ceiling computed by the untouched existing function:

  ```rust
  // resilience.rs — NEW, alongside (not replacing) next_reconnect_delay_ms.
  // Full Jitter: uniform in [0, deterministic_ceiling]. `entropy` is caller-
  // supplied (CSPRNG in production, fixed values in tests) so the fn stays pure.
  // Unbiased range reduction via 128-bit multiply-shift (no modulo bias).
  pub fn next_reconnect_delay_jittered_ms(
      policy: ReconnectPolicy,
      attempt: u32,
      entropy: u64,
  ) -> u64 {
      let ceiling = next_reconnect_delay_ms(policy, attempt);
      ((u128::from(entropy) * (u128::from(ceiling) + 1)) >> 64) as u64
  }
  ```

  Shape justification: a **new function alongside the old**, not a field or breaking change — (1) the deterministic function remains the right tool for spec-timed ladders and IS the jitter ceiling, so it cannot be removed; (2) the existing test stays byte-identical and meaningful (it pins the envelope every jittered draw must fall inside — §2's rule satisfied with zero test churn); (3) injected `entropy` keeps the function pure, making the §5 "seedable RNG" requirement trivial — tests pass literal entropy values, production draws via the CSPRNG-fail-soft pattern already established at `traversal.rs:1632` (per FIS-0010), and on entropy-source failure passes `u64::MAX`, which degrades to exactly the deterministic ceiling (old behavior — fail-soft never *shortens* nor exceeds the envelope; entropy `u64::MAX` maps exactly to `ceiling`, entropy `0` to `0`). Why Full over Equal/Decorrelated Jitter: AWS's own simulation shows Full Jitter with near-lowest total work and completion time; Equal Jitter keeps half the herd synchronization for no benefit; Decorrelated Jitter requires the previous delay as state — it cannot be a pure `(policy, attempt)` function. Reconciliation: FIS-0010's breaker cooldown sketch mentioned decorrelated jitter — recommend it consume THIS primitive instead (full jitter over its exponential cooldown); one shared jittered primitive beats two jitter idioms `[inference]`.

- **Per-site classification and verdicts (§1a/§3b) — every site, migrate-or-leave:**

  | Site | Kind | Verdict |
  |---|---|---|
  | `resilience.rs` primitive | orphaned generic backoff | **extend with jitter** (the only code change) |
  | NAT-PMP `round_trip` (`port_mapper.rs:428`) | receive-timeout ladder, RFC 6886 §3.1 timing | **leave** — no inter-attempt delay exists to jitter; jitter/consolidation would break spec timing; `connect()`-filtered on-LAN gateway, no herd |
  | PCP `round_trip` (`:860`) | receive-timeout ladder, documented RFC 6887 deviation + override | **leave** — same; its RFC even prescribes its own ±10% RAND scheme, a per-protocol concern out of scope |
  | `PortMappingProbe` (`:2404`) | parameter plumbing + sequential fallthrough | **reclassified: not a retry site** |
  | `capture_tunnel_dns_resolution` (`macos_exit_dns_failclosed.rs:601`, 15×2s + 200ms subprocess sub-poll) | local condition-polling | **leave** — backoff is a category error: no contended resource, and growing delays only slow detection |
  | `capture_pf_rules_stdout` (`:438-480`, 15×1s — found by the sweep, same file) | local condition-polling | **leave** — same category |
  | `run_self_check_exchange` (`windows_runtime_boundary.rs:276-322`, 5 attempts, linear `100ms·(n+1)` sleep) | local named-pipe race retry | **leave** — single-process race closure; no herd; migration = churn on a `#[cfg(windows)]` path whose tests pin only the retry *predicates* (`:408/:433/:450`) |
  | `poll_for_macos_rustynet_anchor` (`macos_exit_killswitch_precedence.rs:235`, 15 × fixed interval, compile-time bound `:39`) | local condition-polling | **leave** — pf generation-rotation window; fixed interval correct |
  | `privileged_helper.rs:3509` | test payload iteration | **not a retry site** (§0.4 corrected) |
  | `daemon.rs:9281-9310` (Windows DNS bind, 10 attempts, linear 200ms·(n+1)) | local bind-race retry | **leave** — local socket bind vs SCM restart race; no shared remote, jitter buys nothing `[verified: fact-check]` |
  | `daemon.rs:8902-8927` (host-candidate snapshot, 10×100ms) | local condition-polling | **leave** |
  | CLI/lab tooling class (~35 sites: `retry_root`/`retry_remote_step`/`scp_to`/systemd waiters/vm_lab convergence loops/UTM exec retries/FS `AlreadyExists` collision loops/buffer-size retry) | mixed (i)/(iii)/(iv), all operator-tooling or local | **leave as a class** — single-client lab/ops tooling cannot herd; fixed short sleeps are appropriate; consolidating ~35 sites is churn without a failure mode. New lab helpers MAY adopt the primitive for uniformity `[verified: fact-check — census; inference — verdict]` |
  | `rustynet-control/src/lib.rs:489-503` `register_failure` lockout | duplicate formula, no loop | **leave** — a security lockout SHOULD be deterministic (jitter would let a client shave lockout time), and `rustynet-control` must not grow a dependency on `rustynetd`; noted as the existing evidence that un-adopted primitives get re-implemented |

  **Net migration count: zero.** The honest census finding: the primitive is orphaned not because sites bypassed it, but because **the daemon has no delay-between-attempts network-reconnect loop at all** — reconnect behavior lives in the event-driven reconcile/re-race architecture (1s tick), and every loop that does exist is a spec ladder, a condition-poll, or a local-race retry. The primitive's real consumers are FUTURE: FIS-0010's breaker cooldown (first in line), the relay re-establish path if it ever grows a loop (today it is re-establish-once then fail-closed, `daemon.rs:21537`-pinned), and the mobile client's reconnect logic (the mobile roadmap docs already name reconnect/backoff needs `[verified: fact-check]`). The adoption rule to record: **any new reconnect loop with inter-attempt delays MUST use `next_reconnect_delay_jittered_ms`.**

- **Why it's actually better / honest scale assessment:** the thundering-herd failure mode (shared network event → lockstep retries) is real but MILD at a handful-of-nodes home mesh — tens of packets, not an outage; the one genuinely sensitive target is the relay under synchronized session re-establishment (the relay's pre-auth path is already flagged DoS-sensitive, AUDIT-031), which is exactly the first future consumer's territory. The case for doing the 4-line jitter fix NOW is adoption-readiness: `register_failure` proves the unjittered formula gets copied when the primitive isn't ready-to-hand, and every future caller inherits correct behavior for free. Zero current callers ⇒ zero behavior change today — stated plainly. `[inference]`

- **Ground-rules check (§2):** classify-before-consolidate — done per-site above, with two §0 claims corrected rather than forced. Existing-test preservation — `reconnect_policy_exponential_backoff_is_capped` is untouched and still meaningful (pins the jitter envelope); no silent behavior change anywhere (no caller exists to change). Protocol constraints — NAT-PMP/PCP spec timing untouched (leave verdicts). Cheap — one multiply-shift per retry decision. Safe Rust — pure integer arithmetic, `#![forbid(unsafe_code)]` already at `resilience.rs:1`. Cross-platform — the primitive is pure arithmetic, platform-agnostic by construction; the platform-gated sites all got leave verdicts, so no `cfg` mirroring is needed.

- **What would falsify it:** (1) if a future live-lab relay-restart stage with N clients on the jittered path still shows synchronized re-establish bursts (arrival-time clustering ≈ unjittered), the entropy plumbing is broken or Full Jitter's spread is insufficient at this N — re-examine; (2) if any leave-verdict site later shows a real synchronized-retry incident (e.g., two daemons' Windows DNS bind retries colliding — structurally impossible cross-host, so this would falsify the classification method itself); (3) if the primitive is still caller-less after FIS-0010 lands wired, the "adoption-readiness" argument failed and the honest disposition is deleting the corner, not keeping it. `[inference]`

- **Prior art:** M. Brooker, "Exponential Backoff and Jitter," AWS Architecture Blog, 2015 — Full/Equal/Decorrelated Jitter analysis; Full Jitter = `random_between(0, min(cap, base·2^attempt))`, adopted verbatim. Chiu & Jain 1989 for the AIMD lineage. RFC 6886 §3.1 and RFC 6887 §8.1.1 as the spec-timed ladders deliberately NOT consolidated. Lemire 2019 (fast unbiased bounded random via multiply-shift) for the range reduction. `[inference — citations from knowledge, not re-fetched]`

- **Detailed Recommended Patch Implementation Plan:**
  - **New signature (resilience.rs):** `pub fn next_reconnect_delay_jittered_ms(policy: ReconnectPolicy, attempt: u32, entropy: u64) -> u64` (body above). No changes to `ReconnectPolicy` or `next_reconnect_delay_ms`.
  - **Call-site changes:** none in this pass (zero migrations). Doc-comment cross-references added at the five §0 hand-rolled sites ("deliberately independent — see resilience.rs + FIS-0016 classification") to end the parallel-evolution pattern check e documented.
  - **Existing tests that must keep passing:** `reconnect_policy_exponential_backoff_is_capped` (`resilience.rs:392-402`) — unchanged; `nat_pmp_round_trip_retries_with_exponential_backoff_per_rfc_6886_3_1` (`port_mapper.rs:2919`, asserts Timeout + elapsed ≥ 300ms across 3 doubling attempts); the windows predicate tests (`:408/:433/:450`); `poll_sample_returns_found_immediately_when_anchor_present` / `poll_sample_retries_within_budget_then_gives_up` (`macos_exit_killswitch_precedence.rs:427/:441`) — all untouched by construction `[verified: fact-check]`.
  - **New tests (resilience.rs):** `jittered_delay_never_exceeds_deterministic_ceiling` (entropy ∈ {0, 1, 2³², 2⁶³, u64::MAX} × attempts 0..8: `jittered ≤ next_reconnect_delay_ms(...)`); `jittered_delay_entropy_extremes_map_to_zero_and_ceiling` (entropy 0 ⇒ 0; u64::MAX ⇒ exactly the ceiling); `jittered_delay_cap_holds_at_saturating_attempts` (attempt = u32::MAX); `jittered_delay_spans_distinct_values_deterministically` (fixed entropy set {0, 2⁶², 2⁶³, u64::MAX} yields ≥ 3 distinct values for a ceiling ≥ 4 — deterministic by injected entropy, no statistical flake).
  - **Commit sequence + effort:** 1 (S) the jittered fn + four tests, unwired — pure addition; 2 (S) cross-reference doc comments at the five hand-rolled sites + a one-line adoption rule in `documents/CODE_MAP.md`'s resilience entry; 3 (dependency-ordered, S once FIS-0010 lands) wire the breaker cooldown through `next_reconnect_delay_jittered_ms` as the primitive's first real consumer.

## Focused pass — Considered and rejected / leave-as-is register (retry/backoff)

- **NAT-PMP + PCP `round_trip` migration** — rejected: receive-timeout ladders with zero inter-attempt delay; consolidation would conflate "how long to wait for a response" with "how long to wait before retrying," and jitter would violate RFC 6886 §3.1 / the documented PCP deviation. The formula overlap is coincidence of arithmetic, not of semantics. `[verified: fact-check]` (shape) / `[inference]` (verdict)
- **Condition-poll migrations** (dscacheutil, pf anchors ×2, host-candidate snapshot, systemd waiters, vm_lab convergence loops) — rejected as a category error: polls wait for an async local condition; there is no contended remote to protect and exponential growth only delays detection.
- **Local-race retries** (windows named-pipe self-check, Windows DNS bind) — rejected: single-host races, no herd possible; their linear ramps are already fit for purpose.
- **`register_failure` lockout consolidation** — rejected: deterministic lockout is a security property (jitter would shorten enforced wait), and the dependency direction (control ← rustynetd) forbids it; kept as evidence for the adoption-rule argument.
- **Equal / Decorrelated Jitter** — rejected: Equal retains half the synchronization; Decorrelated requires previous-delay state, breaking the pure-function shape (and FIS-0010 is redirected to consume the Full-Jitter primitive rather than hand-rolling decorrelated).
- **A `jitter: bool` field on `ReconnectPolicy`** — rejected: forces every construction site to decide, silently changes the meaning of the existing fn's test, and entropy still has to come from somewhere — the separate-fn shape is strictly cleaner.

## Focused pass — Coverage note (retry/backoff)

- **Verifier substitution, disclosed:** the tasked `~/.config/opencode/verify.sh` script is not reachable from this session's sandboxed shell (only the project folder is mounted; the script lives in the user's home). The five §4 checks ran instead as independent read-only Sonnet 5 agents against the fresh worktree — same independence intent; `[verified: fact-check]` tags denote those checks.
- The ~35-site CLI/lab tooling class received a class-level verdict, not per-site analysis — a per-site sweep of `vm_lab/` retry helpers was out of budget; none showed herd-shaped exposure in the census, but individual sleeps/attempt counts were not audited for fitness.
- `third_party/` was excluded as vendored; shell scripts under `scripts/` (embedded PowerShell/bash retry loops) were only caught where embedded in Rust string literals.
- RFC 6887's own RAND-based retransmission scheme (which the PCP client deviates from) was noted but not designed for — a per-protocol compliance question, not a consolidation one.
- Worktree used: `origin/main` @ `5868a09`; removed after the pass. Line numbers verified 2026-07-02 against that commit; they will drift.

# Focused pass — CLI argument-parsing standardization — 2026-07-02

> Grounding note: read and verified against fresh `origin/main` (`5868a09`, default branch confirmed `main`) in a disposable worktree (`.claude/worktrees/fable-cliargs`, removed after the pass). Worktree doc tops at FIS-0012; FIS-0013..0016 exist uncommitted in the primary checkout, so this entry takes **FIS-0017**.

## FIS-0017: Do NOT adopt clap — harmonize on the in-house "relay pattern" instead (verdict: clap rejected on a recorded stance + zero evidenced pain; harmonization yes, smallest binary first)

- **Pipeline / area:** CLI entry points of the workspace binaries — `rustynet-nas`, `rustynet-llm-gateway`, `rustynet-relay`, `rustynetd`, `rustynet-cli`, `rustynet-xtask`, `rustynet-lab-monitor`, `rustynet-control` — plus `rustynet-operator`'s existing std-only parser. No trust surface; parser-implementation question only.

- **Grounded problem statement (real scale, corrected against verification):**
  All binaries hand-roll `std::env::args()` parsing, but the §0 rough proxy badly misstated the shape of the problem. Real numbers `[verified: fact-check]`: `rustynet-nas/src/main.rs` = 372 lines with **5 flags** in a 42-line parser (`parse_and_validate_config`, `:84-125`); `rustynet-llm-gateway` = 520 lines, **5 flags**, 62-line parser (`:91-152`); `rustynet-relay` = 3,721 lines with 8 flags + two positional subcommands (`windows-service-hardening-check`, `hello-limiter-audit`) + a `--windows-service` mode, an inline usage text (`main.rs:2062-2073`), and — uniquely — an **argv-injectable parser** (`parse_args_from`, `:1979-2086`) with a real test suite (~10+ parsing tests, `:2396+`); `rustynetd/src/main.rs` = 5,647 lines; `rustynet-cli/src/main.rs` = **24,431 lines** (its `parse_command` at `:1505` plus multiple subcommand dispatch blocks); `rustynet-lab-monitor` parses one flag with no error handling; `rustynet-control`'s main accepts no args at all.
  The real, evidenced defects are NOT "hand-rolling is laborious": (1) `rustynet-nas` and `rustynet-llm-gateway` have **no `--help` at all** and **zero tests** on their parsers — which read `std::env::args()` directly inside the parse function, so they are untestable as written `[verified: fact-check]`; (2) error-message shapes have drifted (`unknown argument {other:?}` in nas/llm vs `unknown argument: {arg}` in relay vs `unknown daemon argument` in rustynetd) `[verified: first-hand]`; (3) the only load-bearing consumers of the nas/llm flag spellings are the systemd `ExecStart` lines (`scripts/systemd/rustynet-nas.service:35-39`, `rustynet-llm-gateway.service:34-38`) — and **nothing anywhere tests that those ExecStart argvs actually parse**, so a flag rename would ship silently `[verified: fact-check]`.

- **The worth-it verdict (§1a): clap — NO. Harmonization — yes, scoped.**
  1. **A deliberate stance is on record, not just accretion:** `StartShOperatorUxRustMigrationPlan_2026-05-24.md` §8 ("Open decisions" #2) explicitly weighed "Manual typed parser … vs. adopting `clap`" and recommended manual "to match the codebase and avoid a new dependency in a security-sensitive surface; revisit if the flag set grows" — and that decision was carried into live code: `crates/rustynet-operator/src/args.rs::parse_start_args` (`:26-82`) + `help_text()` (`:84-95`), std-only, empty `[dependencies]` `[verified: fact-check]`. The revisit trigger ("flag set grows") has not fired for the small binaries (5 flags each).
  2. **clap is NOT "already available":** the lockfile's clap 4.6.1 (+clap_builder 4.6.0, clap_lex 1.1.0, **no clap_derive anywhere**) is pulled solely by `criterion` 0.5.1 — a dev-only benchmark harness declared in exactly two crates' `[dev-dependencies]` (relay, backend-wireguard), both annotated "Dev-only; never in the shipped dependency graph." No workspace crate declares clap; `[workspace.dependencies]` holds only `rand` `[verified: fact-check]`. Production adoption means a NEW direct dependency plus the `clap_derive`/`syn`/`quote` proc-macro chain and `anstream`/`anstyle` — in a workspace that ships zero arg-parsing deps, gates supply chain with `cargo audit`/`cargo deny`, and annotates even dev-only additions.
  3. **Zero evidenced pain:** git history contains no commit mentioning clap, no Cargo.toml ever touched it, and no recurring arg-parsing bug-fix pattern exists `[verified: first-hand — git log greps]`. The general "libraries are better" argument has nothing concrete to stand on here.
  4. **The one place clap would plausibly pay — `rustynet-cli` — is exactly where it's most dangerous:** 24.4k-line main.rs, multi-block subcommand dispatch, and two verified textual-output compatibility constraints elsewhere in the fleet (below) set the tone; a full migration is a multi-week L× undertaking with a regression surface measured in hundreds of flags. Out of scope per §3, ROM below.

- **Compatibility findings (§4d) — what any future migration must preserve `[verified: fact-check]`:**
  - Windows bootstrap PowerShell (`Install-/Verify-/Smoke-RustyNetWindowsService*.ps1`) substring-matches **`rustynetd --help` output** for the literal flags `--windows-service` and `--env-file` — rustynetd's help text is production-load-bearing; a clap-generated help layout would have to keep those substrings (it would, but this is exactly the class of silent coupling that makes the big binaries risky).
  - The vm-lab orchestrator parses **`rustynet anchor list`** row format (`<node_id> capabilities=<csv>`, `role_validation/anchor.rs:142-268`) — a CLI-output contract on rustynet-cli.
  - **`rustynet-nas`/`rustynet-llm-gateway`: nothing anywhere invokes them and parses their output or usage text** (only systemd ExecStart argv) — their wording is unconstrained, which is precisely what makes nas the safe phase-one candidate.

- **The affirmative proposal — harmonize on the relay pattern (in-house, zero new deps):** promote what `rustynet-relay` already does into the workspace convention, applied first to `rustynet-nas`:
  1. argv-injectable parse seam: `fn parse_and_validate_config_from(args: impl IntoIterator<Item = String>) -> Result<Config, String>`, with `main()` passing `std::env::args().skip(1)`;
  2. a `USAGE` constant + `--help`/`-h` handling (exit 0, usage to stderr — matching relay's `:2061-2076` behavior);
  3. unified error shapes: `unknown argument: {arg}` and `missing value for {flag}` (adopting relay's colon form; nas/llm's `{:?}` form changes — safe: no consumer parses their errors `[verified: fact-check]`);
  4. parser unit tests including a **systemd-ExecStart parity test**: parse the exact argv shape from the unit file template (with placeholder values) and assert success — closing the verified silent-drift gap;
  5. a snapshot test pinning the `--help` text so future changes are deliberate.
  For comparison, the clap-derive equivalent for nas would be ~15 lines (`#[derive(Parser)] struct NasArgs { #[arg(long)] bind: SocketAddr, #[arg(long)] data_root: PathBuf, #[arg(long)] access_dir: PathBuf, #[arg(long)] at_rest_key_credential: Option<String>, #[arg(long)] at_rest_key_file: Option<PathBuf> }`) — the code saving is real but small (≈40 lines), and it cannot outweigh the dependency-chain cost against a recorded stance `[inference]`.

- **Phase-one candidate (§1b): `rustynet-nas`** — smallest flag set (5), zero external consumers of its output/usage/errors, zero existing parser tests to break, and its at-rest-key handling makes parser test coverage genuinely valuable (a mis-parsed `--at-rest-key-file` is a security-adjacent failure). `rustynet-llm-gateway` follows as phase two (same shape); `rustynet-relay` is already conformant (it IS the pattern); `rustynet-lab-monitor` (workspace-excluded, 1 flag) optional; `rustynetd`/`rustynet-cli` explicitly untouched.

- **Cost/tradeoffs:** zero new dependencies; phase-one adds ~60-100 lines to nas (help text + tests) while restructuring ~42 — honest accounting: total LoC goes UP; the measured win is testability, `--help` existence, and drift protection, not raw line count. Compile-time/binary-size impact: none (vs. clap's proc-macro chain, which measurably inflates cold builds and adds ~200-400KB per binary `[inference — not measured here]`).

- **Ground-rules check (§3):** phase one touches neither `rustynet-cli` nor `rustynetd` — PASS. Every existing flag name/required-ness preserved exactly; only the unknown-arg error wording unifies (verified consumer-free) — PASS with that one disclosed delta. Output-parsing consumers checked before proposing (§4d) — PASS. Safe Rust — trivially PASS. Measurement plan — below, PASS.

- **Measurement plan (required):** track in the owning ledger per binary: (a) parser test count (nas: 0 → ≥8) and whether an ExecStart-parity test exists (0 → 1 per service binary); (b) `--help` presence (3/8 binaries today → 8/8 target for the service binaries); (c) diff stat of parsing+usage regions per migration commit; (d) drift incidents caught by the parity/snapshot tests over the following quarter — if that number is 0 after two quarters AND no new flags landed, the harmonization beyond nas/llm was over-engineering and phases 3+ should stop.

- **What would falsify it:** (1) the verdict itself: a future audit finding real arg-parsing bugs recurring across binaries (git shows none today) or flag sets growing past ~15-20/binary — the recorded "revisit if the flag set grows" trigger fires and clap should be re-evaluated honestly; (2) the phase-one plan: if the nas migration takes >1 day or breaks any consumer (there should be none), the "safe smallest first" premise was wrong; (3) if the ExecStart-parity + help-snapshot tests catch nothing in 6 months and no flags change, stop at nas/llm.

- **Prior art:** the project's own precedent, twice over: `rustynet-relay`'s `parse_args_from` (argv-injectable + tested + usage text) and `rustynet-operator::args::parse_start_args` (the recorded manual-over-clap decision, landed). External: `pico-args`/`lexopt` as the minimal-dep middle ground — noted and rejected: still a new dependency, saving ~30 lines/binary `[inference]`.
