- **Detailed Recommended Patch Implementation Plan (phase one, `rustynet-nas` only):**
  - **Refactor:** `parse_and_validate_config()` (`main.rs:84-125`) → `parse_and_validate_config_from(args: impl IntoIterator<Item = String>) -> Result<Config, String>` + thin `main()` wrapper; add `const USAGE: &str` naming all 5 flags with the either/or key rule; add `--help`/`-h` arm (usage → stderr, exit 0); unify error strings to `unknown argument: {arg}` / `missing value for {flag}`.
  - **Exact parity requirements:** flags `--bind` (required, SocketAddr), `--data-root` (required, path), `--access-dir` (required, path), `--at-rest-key-credential` / `--at-rest-key-file` (exactly one required — rule at `main.rs:145-160`); no short forms exist today and none are added; required-flag error wording (`--bind is required` etc.) preserved verbatim `[verified: fact-check — flag census]`.
  - **Existing tests that must keep passing:** none exist for this parser `[verified: fact-check]`; the crate's store/protocol/health tests are untouched; the CI gate `scripts/ci/nas_default_deny_gates.sh` greps symbols + runs `store::tests`/`protocol::tests` — unaffected.
  - **New tests:** `nas_args_parse_full_valid_argv`; `nas_args_each_required_flag_missing_errors_verbatim`; `nas_args_key_source_exactly_one_required`; `nas_args_unknown_argument_rejected`; `nas_args_missing_value_rejected`; `nas_args_help_flag_short_and_long`; `nas_args_systemd_execstart_shape_parses` (the argv from `rustynet-nas.service:35-39` with placeholder values); `nas_args_help_text_snapshot`.
  - **Commit sequence + effort:** 1 (S) the nas refactor + all eight tests, help text reviewed line-by-line against the flag census; 2 (S, separate later decision after nas is live-proven) the identical treatment for `rustynet-llm-gateway` (+ its ExecStart parity test); 3 (explicitly NOT planned here) any consideration of `rustynetd`/`rustynet-cli`. **ROM for full `rustynet-cli` clap migration (order-of-magnitude only, NOT recommended, NOT planned):** 24,431-line main.rs, multi-block dispatch, hundreds of distinct flags, two live textual-output contracts — realistically multiple weeks (L × 5-10) with per-subcommand regression testing; recorded here solely so the scale is visible.

## Focused pass — Considered and rejected (CLI parsing)

- **Adopting clap (any tier: derive or builder)** — rejected on the combination of: a recorded, deliberate manual-over-clap decision for security-sensitive surfaces (`StartShOperatorUxRustMigrationPlan_2026-05-24.md` §8, landed as `rustynet-operator/src/args.rs`) `[verified: fact-check]`; zero evidenced parsing pain in the entire git history `[verified: first-hand]`; the proc-macro dependency chain landing in production binaries of a workspace that currently ships zero arg-parsing deps and flags even dev-only additions; and savings of ~40 lines per small binary. The revisit trigger is recorded and honest: flag-set growth.
- **`pico-args`/`lexopt` as a minimal-dep compromise** — rejected: still a new production dependency for a ~30-line saving; the in-house pattern already exists twice.
- **Consolidating all binaries onto `rustynet-operator::args`** — rejected: `parse_start_args` is purpose-built for the operator-menu flag set, not a generic engine; generalizing it into a shared parsing framework recreates a clap-shaped abstraction in-house without clap's maturity — the CONVENTION (seam + usage + tests + error shapes) is what's shared, not a framework `[inference]`.
- **Any phase-one touch of `rustynet-cli`/`rustynetd`** — rejected per §3 and per the two verified output-compatibility contracts (rustynetd `--help` substrings; `anchor list` row format).

# Focused pass — STUN candidate-gathering concurrency + policy-evaluator worth-it check — 2026-07-02

> Grounding note: read and verified against fresh `origin/main` (`5868a09`, default branch confirmed `main`) in a disposable worktree (`.claude/worktrees/fable-stun-policy`, removed after the pass). Worktree doc tops at FIS-0012; FIS-0013..0017 exist uncommitted in the primary checkout, so Part A takes **FIS-0018**. Part B's verdict is "not worth it" and is recorded under Considered-and-rejected per the pass charter.

## FIS-0018: Batched-send / single-receiver STUN gathering with a true gather deadline (no threads, no async — and a budget-sliced serial fallback for the singleton round-trip path)

- **Pipeline / area:** `crates/rustynetd/src/stun_client.rs` (`gather_mapped_endpoints` :89-106, `gather_mapped_endpoints_with_round_trip` :110-146), consumers in `daemon.rs::poll_stun_results` (:5191-5236) and `dataplane_candidates.rs::gather_srflx_for_family` (:333-358). Pure latency/scheduling; packet formats, tx-id echo validation, and dedup semantics unchanged.

- **Grounded problem statement (with two corrections to the brief):**
  - Both gather functions loop `for server in &self.servers` fully serially, one complete round trip (with a per-server timeout) before the next server is contacted `[verified: subagent]`.
  - **`--traversal-stun-gather-timeout-ms` is misnamed today:** its default is 2,000ms (`TRAVERSAL_DEFAULT_STUN_GATHER_TIMEOUT_MS`, `traversal.rs:62`, re-exported `daemon.rs:293`) and it is consumed as the **per-server** timeout (`StunClient { timeout }` → `set_read_timeout` per query at `stun_client.rs:171`, and per-server closure arg at `:124`). **No overall bound on the multi-server loop exists anywhere** — N configured servers cost up to N×2s worst case `[verified: subagent]`.
  - **Correction 1 (call-path):** `dataplane_candidates.rs:357` is real and socket-based, but its caller chain (`gather_candidate_set`, :397) currently has **no production wiring** — only unit tests and a doc reference. The LIVE production path is `poll_stun_results` (`daemon.rs:5191`, fired from both main-loop variants at :9540/:9766 on a 60s refresh timer) → `gather_mapped_endpoints_with_round_trip` → the backend's `authoritative_transport_round_trip` `[verified: subagent]`. That call runs **on the daemon's single main thread** (no tokio/async anywhere in rustynetd `[verified: subagent]`) — so a multi-server config stalls the entire IPC/DNS/reconcile loop up to N×2s per refresh. The second production consumer is the CLI preflight (`ops_cross_network_preflight.rs:264`).
  - **Correction 2 (structural constraint the brief didn't know):** the authoritative round-trip transport is a hard **singleton** — `outstanding_round_trip: Option<_>` with an explicit second-round-trip rejection (`userspace_shared/runtime.rs:571/:612`; macOS mirror `:635/:677`) `[verified: subagent]`. True concurrency through `_with_round_trip` is structurally impossible without redesigning that primitive (out of scope; deliberately shaped that way per the FIS-0013 pass).
  - **Honesty about current configs:** there is **no default STUN server list** — the flag defaults to empty (gathering entirely off, `daemon.rs:1676/:3888-3894`), and every in-repo example uses 0 or 1 servers `[verified: subagent]`. The multi-server case this pass optimizes is supported-but-not-yet-exercised; it becomes the recommended shape once FIS-0009's NAT classification (which requires ≥2 servers' observations) is wired.
  - Also verified: production always passes `Some(socket)` to `gather_mapped_endpoints` (the `None` mode is one test with an empty server list) `[verified: subagent]`.

- **Named mechanism:** two mechanisms matched to the two entry points' actual constraints, sharing one semantics:
  1. **Socket path (`gather_mapped_endpoints`) — batched-send + single-receiver demux.** NOT thread-per-server: concurrent `recv` on one shared socket misdelivers responses across threads (any thread's recv gets any datagram), and the production socket IS shared `[inference from verified socket usage]`. Instead: resolve all servers; send all binding requests back-to-back from the one socket (each with its own tx-id); then ONE receive loop until `deadline = now + self.timeout`, demuxing each datagram by **source address == a queried target** plus the existing per-request **tx-id echo check** (`parse_binding_response`), filling a per-server-index slot table. Output is then assembled **in server order** (not arrival order) with the exact existing dedup predicate — so whenever all servers respond, the result is byte-identical to the serial version, deterministically. Zero threads, zero new dependencies, no `Send` bounds — the §A2 `FnMut`-not-`Send` concern dissolves entirely. Side benefit: source-address matching makes the socket path exactly as strict as the round-trip variant's existing `remote_addr != target` rejection (`:127-129`) — today's socket path accepts a datagram from anywhere that echoes the tx-id `[verified: fact-check — no source check in the socket path today]`.
  2. **Round-trip path (`_with_round_trip`) — budget-sliced serial.** The singleton transport forces sequential queries, so the fix is deadline accounting: total budget = `self.timeout`; each server's round trip gets `min(self.timeout, budget / servers.len())` — i.e. N=1 gets the full timeout (byte-identical to today), N=3 gets ~666ms each, total ≤ one gather deadline. RFC 5389's default initial RTO is 500ms, so a 666ms slice comfortably covers a healthy public STUN server's RTT; an unresponsive server can no longer eat other servers' budget or stall the main loop beyond 1× deadline. `FnMut` signature unchanged.
  With both, the flag finally means what its name says: **total gather wall-clock ≤ `--traversal-stun-gather-timeout-ms`** regardless of server count.

- **Why it's actually better (quantified with the real defaults):** with the verified 2s per-server default and 3 configured servers: today's worst case (all unreachable) = **6s of main-thread stall** per 60s refresh; one unreachable of three ≈ 2.1s (RTT + full 2s + RTT). Batched: **≤2s worst case, typically ~1 RTT (50-150ms)** when servers respond — and the daemon main loop (IPC, DNS resolver, reconcile) is never blocked longer than one deadline. The round-trip path drops from N×2s worst case to ≤2s. Single-server configs (today's only real configs) are unchanged in both timing and results `[inference — arithmetic on verified constants]`.

- **Cost / tradeoffs:** no new threads, tasks, or dependencies; the socket path's complexity moves from "N sequential mini-transactions" to "one send loop + one demux loop + a slot table" (~40 net new lines); the `StunQuerySocket` test-seam trait gains send-to/recv-from-shaped methods. Behavior deltas to disclose: (a) round-trip path multi-server per-server timeout shrinks from `timeout` to `timeout/N` (deliberate — that IS the fix; single-server unchanged); (b) socket-path `None` mode (test-only, verified) binds one ephemeral socket for the whole batch instead of one per server; (c) socket path now rejects responses from unqueried sources (a strictness increase, security-positive). A slow-but-responding server that answers after the deadline is dropped where serial might have caught it — mitigated by the deadline being operator-tunable, and symmetric with today's per-server timeout drop `[inference]`.

- **Ground-rules check (§A2):** single-server invisible — PASS (one request, one recv, same timeout, same result; both variants). Dedup semantics — PASS (identical predicate, applied in deterministic server order). Concurrency style matches the codebase — PASS-plus (rustynetd has no async runtime `[verified: subagent]`; the design needs no threads either — it out-minimalizes the thread-per-server assumption; `spawn_local_stun_echo`'s thread stays test-only). Overall deadline — PASS (that is the centerpiece). Safe Rust — PASS. `FnMut` Send-safety — resolved by construction (no cross-thread execution anywhere).

- **What would falsify it:** (1) a loopback bench showing batched N=3 gather NOT materially faster than serial when one server is blackholed (should be ~2s vs ~4.1s — if not, the demux loop is broken); (2) if no deployment ever configures ≥2 servers after FIS-0009's classifier lands (which needs ≥2), the change was premature scaffolding — measurable by grepping shipped configs; (3) any observed result-set difference vs the serial version on all-responsive fixtures (would falsify the determinism claim and the migration's safety).

- **Detailed Recommended Patch Implementation Plan:**
  - **Signatures: both public signatures UNCHANGED** (`gather_mapped_endpoints(&self, socket: Option<&UdpSocket>) -> Vec<StunResult>`; `gather_mapped_endpoints_with_round_trip<F: FnMut(SocketAddr, &[u8], Duration) -> Result<StunTransportRoundTrip, String>>(&self, round_trip: F) -> Vec<StunResult>`). Internal additions: `struct PendingQuery { server_index: usize, target: SocketAddr, tx_id: [u8; 12] }`; `fn per_server_slice(&self) -> Duration`; `StunQuerySocket` gains `send_to`/`recv_from`-shaped methods (the existing trait at `stun_client.rs:165+` is the seam).
  - **Collection mechanism, concretely:** `slots: Vec<Option<StunResult>>` indexed by server position; recv loop sets `set_read_timeout(Some(deadline - now))` before each recv; on datagram: find pending entry by source address, verify via the existing `parse_binding_response(&buf, &tx_id)`, fill slot, remove pending; loop ends on deadline, empty pending, or socket error; assemble output by slot order applying the existing dedup `any()` predicate.
  - **Call sites:** none change — `daemon.rs:5207-5224` and `dataplane_candidates.rs:356-357` and `ops_cross_network_preflight.rs:264` compile untouched; `daemon.rs` doc comments + `main.rs` flag help text updated to describe the flag as the total gather deadline (safe: the only load-bearing `--help` substrings are rustynetd's `--windows-service`/`--env-file`, per FIS-0017 `[verified: subagent]`).
  - **Existing tests that must keep passing (named, `[verified: subagent]`):** the stun_client parser suite (all `stun_parser_*` :658-948 incl. `stun_parser_rejects_response_with_wrong_transaction_id` :699), `test_gather_mapped_endpoints_returns_vec_of_socket_addr` :473, `test_gather_mapped_endpoints_with_round_trip_uses_authoritative_local_addr` :483 (single server ⇒ full timeout — unchanged by slicing), `test_gather_mapped_endpoints_uses_provided_socket_identity` :525, `d2_stun_v4/v6_discovered_port_equals_bound_socket_port` :1000/:1036, daemon `daemon_runtime_authoritative_stun_refresh_uses_backend_shared_transport_identity` :21251 (single server), preflight `cone_nat_likely_when_all_stun_servers_agree` :628 and `one_responsive_one_unreachable_yields_mixed_nat_could_work` :654.
  - **New tests (closing verified gaps — no multi-server StunClient test exists at all today `[verified: subagent]`):** `multi_server_gather_completes_within_one_gather_deadline` (two `spawn_local_stun_echo` servers + one RFC 5737 blackhole; assert both results present and elapsed < 2× per-server timeout); `multi_server_gather_dedups_identical_mapped_endpoints` (two echoes reporting the same mapped endpoint ⇒ 1 result); `multi_server_gather_output_is_server_order_not_arrival_order`; `single_server_gather_behavior_unchanged` (result + timing envelope vs old semantics); `batched_gather_ignores_response_from_unqueried_source`; `round_trip_gather_slices_budget_across_servers` (mock closure asserts received timeout == total/N); `round_trip_gather_single_server_receives_full_timeout`.
  - **Commit sequence + effort:** 1 (S) the batched socket-path rewrite + trait seam + its five tests; 2 (S) the budget-sliced round-trip path + its two tests + flag-doc updates; 3 (S, optional) adopt the batched path in `ops_cross_network_preflight`'s per-family probe loop (it currently builds one single-server client per server serially — same win shape for preflight wall-clock). Total: **S-M**.

## Focused pass — Considered and rejected (STUN + policy)

- **Part B verdict: policy/ACL evaluator linear scan — NOT worth optimizing. Closed.** The census `[verified: subagent]` is unambiguous on both §B1 axes:
  - **Frequency:** zero per-packet call sites exist. The dataplane crates (`rustynet-backend-wireguard`, `rustynet-relay`) and `rustynet-nas` have **no dependency on `rustynet-policy` at all**; nas/llm per-frame admission is a plain lookup against daemon-pre-materialized `grants.v1` files, never the evaluator. Every real call site is admission-time (exit-node selection `phase10.rs:5300`, LAN-route grant `:5376`), signed-state-refresh/reconcile time (`service_access_state.rs:90` materialization, `daemon.rs:4106-4143` auto-tunnel gating), or operator-driven artifact issuance / audit / CLI (`rustynet-control/src/lib.rs:3442`, `policy_default_deny_audit.rs`).
  - **Rule count:** the daemon constructs exactly **one** hardcoded rule (`daemon.rs:3763-3775`); CLI-issued sets contain one rule per hand-typed `--allow` pair; no generator fans out nodes×services; no max-rule constant, no 100+-rule test or bench exists anywhere; the documented scale bar is 2-50 nodes. Realistic rule sets are single digits to a few dozen.
  - A linear first-match scan over ≤dozens of rules at reconcile/admission frequency costs nanoseconds; an indexed structure would add real risk (first-match-wins precedence is semantic — `lib.rs:131-155` — and default-deny falls out of the scan's fallthrough) for zero measurable gain. **Re-open triggers, recorded so nobody re-proposes this blind:** a per-packet caller appearing; programmatic rule generation (nodes×services fan-out) landing; or rule counts exceeding ~1,000.
- **Thread-per-server STUN gathering** — rejected: broken on the shared production socket (cross-thread response misdelivery), needs `Send` bounds on the round-trip closure, and adds thread overhead a single-threaded demux loop makes unnecessary. `[inference]`
- **Making `_with_round_trip` truly concurrent** — rejected: the authoritative round-trip transport is a verified singleton that rejects overlapping round trips by design (`runtime.rs:571`); redesigning it is FIS-0013-adjacent transport surgery, not a gathering optimization.
- **Moving STUN gathering off the main thread entirely** — noted as the bigger fix for main-loop stalls generally, deferred: it changes daemon threading architecture; the deadline bound (≤2s) makes the stall acceptable at the 60s refresh cadence. `[inference]`

## Focused pass — Coverage note (STUN + policy)

- **Verifier note:** per the operator's standing instruction (2026-07-02), verification for this and future passes uses the environment's native read-only subagents (one narrow question per call), tagged `[verified: subagent]`. The DeepSeek MCP / `opencode` routes are dropped as unreachable from this session's sandbox (the MCP reports no API key — an `/mcp` reconnect on the host would be needed if it's ever wanted again). The five §5 checks for this pass ran as five independent subagent reads against the worktree.

# Focused pass — formal verification of the trust-state protocol — 2026-07-02

> Grounding note: read and verified against fresh `origin/main` (`5868a09`, default branch confirmed `main`) in a disposable worktree (`.claude/worktrees/fable-formal-verify`, removed after the pass). Primary-doc numbering continues: this pass takes **FIS-0019**. This pass EXECUTES the first two phases of FIS-0002's build path (which proposed exactly this spec and was reviewed accept-with-fixes) — it is the delivery, not a competing proposal.

## FIS-0019: Machine-checkable TLA+ model of `apply_signed_update` — delivered, with a bounded model-checking result that re-finds RSA-0009

**Artifacts (the deliberate multi-file exception, per the pass charter):** [`documents/formal/MembershipTrustState.tla`](../../formal/MembershipTrustState.tla) (the spec), [`documents/formal/MembershipTrustState.cfg`](../../formal/MembershipTrustState.cfg) (TLC configuration — required to actually run it, hence included), and [`documents/formal/membership_trust_state_explorer.py`](../../formal/membership_trust_state_explorer.py) (an exhaustive BFS surrogate that mirrors the spec transition-for-transition, included because TLC itself was unreachable from the authoring sandbox — see the model-checking result below; the `.tla` is canonical).

- **Pipeline / area:** `crates/rustynet-control/src/membership.rs` — `apply_signed_update` (:693-737), `reduce_membership_state` (:1141-1253), `MembershipReplayCache::observe` (:552-562). Zero code changes; design-time verification artifact only.

- **Grounded problem statement (with three corrections to the pass brief):**
  - The guard chain is confirmed byte-precise and in this exact order `[verified: subagent]`: `state.validate()` (:699) → `record.canonical_payload()` (:701 — **not a mere serializer**: it independently enforces `epoch_new == epoch_prev+1` (:421-425) and `created_at < expires_at` (:426-430), the latter enforced ONLY here on this path) → network-id (:702) → expiry (:707) → clock-skew, `MEMBERSHIP_CLOCK_SKEW_SECS = 90` (:23, :710) → `prev_state_root` (:713) → epoch chain (:716) → `verify_membership_signatures` (:722) → reduce with **the signed record's `created_at_unix`** (:727, the RSA-0009 fix comment :724-726) → `next.epoch = epoch_new` (:728) → `next.validate()` (:729) → recomputed-root equality (:730-733) → `replay_cache.observe` **last** (:734; observe checks seen-id AND `epoch_new <= max_epoch` before mutating either — a failed observe leaves the cache intact).
  - **Correction 1:** `MembershipOperation` has **8** variants, not 5 — the brief missed `RemoveNode` (:347), `RotateApprover` (:360), `SetQuorum` (:361) `[verified: subagent]`.
  - **Correction 2:** three of the six "existing tests" named in the brief (`pre_rotation_bundle…`, `replayed_old_epoch_bundle…`, `bundle_with_unknown_epoch_tag…`, membership.rs:3379-3441) pin `verify_epoch_tagged_bundle` (:1104-1127) — a **separate key-rotation subsystem that is currently unwired in production** (only its own tests call it; MasterWorkPlan records it as "ready to be consumed") `[verified: subagent]`. Its properties belong to a future key-rotation pass, not this one.
  - **Correction 3 (scope call per §1):** `verify_membership_signatures` (:999-1040) is a self-contained boolean gate (duplicate-signer rejection, distinct-signer count ≥ `quorum_threshold`, active-approver membership, per-signature Ed25519, owner-role flag required only for `RotateApprover`/`SetQuorum` per `requires_owner_signer` :380-385) `[verified: subagent]` — cheap to abstract as the oracle §1 prescribes. The approver-mutating operations themselves (`RotateApprover` upsert :1231-1242, `SetQuorum` :1243-1250, plus `validate()`'s quorum≤active-approvers coupling) are a real second dimension and are **deferred** with the quorum arithmetic.
  - The RSA-0009 story confirmed from the reducer's own comment (:1129-1140): the reducer previously stamped `unix_now()` instead of the signed timestamp, so producer-computed and applier-recomputed roots diverged whenever apply-second ≠ mint-second — `RevokeNode`/`RestoreNode`/`RotateNodeKey`/`SetNodeCapabilities` **could never apply**; AddNode (fields carried in the record) and RemoveNode (no stamp) were unaffected, which is why the mesh looked functional while revocation was silently dead.

- **The model (real → abstract mapping, each choice's faithfulness):** state variables `epoch`, and per-node `status`/`caps`/`key`/`updated` parallel functions (the roster); the **state root is the state tuple itself** — faithful because `state_root_hex` is SHA-256 over `canonical_payload`, which covers the FULL state content including every node's `updated_at_unix` (:246-305, :307-310 `[verified: subagent]`), and hashing is injective modulo collisions (abstracted away); `RemoveNode` normalizes the slot to canonical absent values (the analog of fields vanishing from the payload). Replay cache = `seenIds ⊆ UpdateIds` + `maxEpochSeen ∈ Nat`, exactly `MembershipReplayCache`'s two fields. Signatures = `verified ∈ BOOLEAN` on the record (§1 oracle). Producer (`preview_next_state`) always stamps `created_at`; the applier's re-derivation stamps `IF BuggyReducer THEN now ELSE created_at` — `CONSTANT BuggyReducer` reintroduces RSA-0009 exactly, confined to the four stamping arms. The in-scope `validate()` rule "active ⇒ ≥1 capability" (:1699-1704) is modeled (it makes `RestoreNode`-after-caps-emptied rejectable — a real corner `[verified: subagent]`); capability-pairing rules are not. Adversary alphabet: unsigned honest-shaped records, byte-replays of previously-accepted records, and payload-consistent epoch-skips (the `apply_signed_update_rejects_epoch_chain_break` shape).
- **The properties (formal, in the module; glosses + test tracebacks):**
  - `InvLogEpochsChain` — every accepted update advances the epoch by exactly 1 and consecutive acceptances link. ↔ `apply_signed_update_rejects_epoch_chain_break` (:2593-2618) + `replay_and_rollback_are_rejected` (:2296-2333).
  - `InvNoDoubleAccept` — no `update_id` accepted twice. ↔ `replay_and_rollback_are_rejected`.
  - `InvHonestNeverRootMismatch` — an honest, fresh, chained, signed record is never rejected for recomputed-root divergence. **The RSA-0009 catcher — new: no existing Rust test pins this** (the three core apply tests are all AddNode-based, the one arm the historical bug did NOT affect, so none would catch its reintroduction `[inference from the verified test census]`).
  - `InvNoForkPerRoot` — each base state (root) is extended by at most one accepted update; no divergent fork from a shared parent. ↔ the `prev_state_root` guard + the replay test's second half.
  - `InvCacheCoupling` + action properties `RejectLeavesCacheIntact`, `EpochNeverDecreases` — the watermark tracks exactly the accepted frontier and any rejection leaves the cache byte-identical. ↔ `replay_cache_not_updated_on_failed_update` (:2416-2467, which corrupts `new_state_root` then successfully retries the same `update_id` — the cache-poisoning ordering bug this guards).
- **Model-checking result (§2c) — honest tooling disclosure:** **TLC itself could not run in the authoring sandbox**: Java 11 is present, but every `tla2tools.jar` distribution host is blocked by the network allowlist (github release assets, Maven Central, `nightly.tlapl.us`, INRIA — all connection-reset; attempted and logged). Per the pass rules this is reported, not papered over: the `.tla` module is delivered unrun by TLC. To still attach a real result, the companion Python explorer executes the identical transition system (same constants as the `.cfg`) exhaustively:
  - **Correct reducer (`BuggyReducer = FALSE`): all 5 invariants + both action properties hold over the full reachable bounded space — 11,446 states, 21,020 transitions, 2,288 accepting applies.**
  - **Buggy variant (`BuggyReducer = TRUE`): `InvHonestNeverRootMismatch` violated, minimal counterexample = `MintHonest → Tick → ApplyReject`** — an honest `SetNodeCapabilities`-class record minted at T=1, wall clock advances to T=2, applier re-derivation stamps T=2 ≠ signed T=1, roots diverge, `NewStateRootMismatch`. The buggy run still recorded 110 accepting applies (AddNode/RemoveNode/same-tick arms) — reproducing the historical bug's exact blast-radius signature: the mesh keeps working, revocation silently doesn't.
  - The model therefore both **retroactively catches RSA-0009** and passes the §5 falsification gate (a model that blessed the broken variant would have been reported as a failed pass).
- **Sync-with-implementation plan (§2d) — the part that keeps this honest:** `proptest`/`stateright`/`kani` are absent from the entire workspace (all Cargo.tomls + lockfiles `[verified: subagent]`); `rustynet-control`'s dev-deps are `tempfile` + the internal alloc-meter only; the existing convention is hand-rolled fixed-count loops, and the two membership fuzz targets are decode-only. Fitting that convention (and FIS-0017's recorded new-dependency posture), the primary proposal is **dependency-free bounded-exhaustive conformance tests** in `rustynet-control` that drive the REAL `apply_signed_update`/`reduce_membership_state` (real Ed25519 test keys, as the existing fixtures already do) over the same small domains the model uses, asserting the same five invariants after every step — a mini-model-check of the real code, in `crates/rustynet-control/tests/membership_model_conformance.rs`: `membership_bounded_exhaustive_invariants_hold` (M), plus the single most valuable direct pin the suite currently lacks: `membership_stamping_ops_apply_at_later_wall_clock` (S) — mint a `RevokeNode`/`SetNodeCapabilities`/`RotateNodeKey`/`RestoreNode` record at T, apply at T+Δ, assert success (this alone would have caught RSA-0009). Optional second layer: `proptest` as a flagged dev-only dependency (the `criterion` precedent) for randomized-with-shrinking coverage — explicitly a separate decision. Discipline rule recorded in the module header: the `.tla`, the `.cfg`, the explorer, and the conformance test share constants and must move together; the conformance test is the CI-enforced one.
- **Ground-rules check (§3):** real guard ordering and exact conditions — PASS (all thirteen steps modeled in order, skew constant included, observe-last preserved; the one omission, the network-id guard, is vacuous in a single-network model and disclosed). Signature crypto abstracted as an oracle — PASS. TLC unavailability reported explicitly — PASS (§2c above). Property tests reuse the real functions — PASS by construction of the §2d plan. Research-only: no `.rs` touched, nothing committed.
- **What would falsify this pass's value:** the buggy-variant run finding nothing (it found the violation in 432 states); the conformance tests (once landed) passing against a deliberately re-broken reducer (would mean the executable sync layer lost the property); or TLC — once run on the real toolchain — disagreeing with the surrogate explorer (would mean the mirror drifted; the `.cfg` is included precisely so this one-command check is cheap on any dev machine).
- **Effort for the deferred scope (future-work ROM, not a commitment):** approver-quorum + `RotateApprover`/`SetQuorum` modeling: M-L (adds a second roster + owner-gating to the alphabet); key-rotation/`verify_epoch_tagged_bundle` + `VerifierArchive`/`PerEpochReplayWatermark` (its own small state machine, currently unwired): L, its own pass; gossip dissemination / multi-applier fork-consistency: L+ (this is FableForkConsistentMembershipTransparency territory); enrollment tokens: M.

## Focused pass — Considered and rejected / not modeled (formal verification)

- **Alloy instead of TLA+** — TLC's exhaustive bounded exploration of a sequential guard-chain transition system with temporal action properties (`RejectLeavesCacheIntact`) is the exact fit; Alloy's relational strengths buy nothing here. Default confirmed, not silently taken. `[inference]`
- **Network-id mismatch guard** — vacuous in a single-network model; modeling two networks doubles the constant space to prove a string comparison. Disclosed omission.
- **Capability-pairing validate() rules** (blind_exit⇒exit_server etc.) — roster-validation richness orthogonal to chain/replay/determinism mechanics; the one validate() rule that interacts with the modeled ops (active⇒nonempty caps) IS modeled. Deferred to the approver/roster pass.
- **`RotateApprover`/`SetQuorum` + quorum counting** — a second governed roster with owner-gating; the signature ORACLE abstraction stays sound because `verify_membership_signatures` consumes only plain state data `[verified: subagent]`, but modeling the roster's own mutation doubles the model for properties this pass doesn't state. Deferred with an M-L estimate.
- **Modeling hash collisions** — the root-is-the-state abstraction deliberately assumes collision-freedom; SHA-256 collision resistance is a cryptographic assumption outside the model's ambit (same class as the signature oracle).

## Focused pass — Coverage note (formal verification)

- TLC was not run (network-blocked toolchain — full detail in §2c above); the surrogate explorer's result stands in until anyone with the jar runs `java -cp tla2tools.jar tlc2.TLC -config MembershipTrustState.cfg MembershipTrustState.tla` (~seconds at these bounds). The `.tla` has also therefore not been machine-parsed — a first TLC run may surface syntax-level fixes; the semantics are pinned by the explorer.
- `documents/README.md`'s docs-tree index does not yet know about `documents/formal/` — index update left for the landing commit (this pass doesn't touch further files).
- The bootstrap seeding path (`replay_membership_snapshot_and_log` :906-932 seeds `max_epoch = snapshot.epoch` with an EMPTY seen-set; daemon/CLI rebuild caches by re-observing log entries `[verified: subagent]`) is faithfully representable but not modeled this pass — the model starts from a fresh cache; a snapshot-resume variant is a cheap future extension.
- Liveness (an honest update is eventually applied under fairness) is deliberately not asserted — this pass is safety-only; the buggy variant is caught via the safety invariant instead.
- Method: five subagent checks ran (guard chain byte-accuracy incl. canonical_payload's hidden validations; replay-cache semantics + the six named tests; approver/quorum complexity for the scope call; proptest/fuzz census; TLC availability probed first-hand). Three §0 corrections resulted (8 ops not 5; three named tests belong to the unwired key-rotation subsystem; canonical_payload validates). Line numbers verified 2026-07-02 against `5868a09`; they will drift.

# Focused pass — gossip anti-entropy + continuous path-quality monitoring — 2026-07-02

> Grounding note: worked against fresh `origin/main` @ `b79cac1` in a disposable worktree (`.claude/worktrees/fable-gossip-path`, removed after the pass; default branch confirmed `main`). `b79cac1` is a merge whose tree is **byte-identical to `5868a09`** (`git diff --name-only 5868a09..b79cac1` = empty `[verified: own-tools]`), so every line number verified in prior passes remains valid. Primary-doc numbering continues: Part A = **FIS-0020**, Part B = **FIS-0021**. External-review routing per the pass charter: both provisioned vendors (ZenMux, NaraRouter) are unreachable from this sandbox (curl status 000 — egress allowlist, same class as the TLC-jar hosts in FIS-0019), so both §5e/§5f reviews ran on the sanctioned last-resort path and are tagged `[reviewed: native-subagent]`. No provisioned key was written to any file or artifact.

## FIS-0020: Digest-first gossip heartbeat + conditional membership bundle-pull (an FIS-0003 amendment plus one new wire nicety, hardened by adversarial review)

- **Pipeline / area:** `crates/rustynetd/src/gossip_runtime.rs` (`maybe_mint_and_broadcast`), `peer_gossip.rs` (wire), and the anchor bundle-pull TCP protocol (`daemon.rs:1004-1145`). Dissemination efficiency only; zero changes to how any received bundle is validated or applied.

- **Relationship to FIS-0003:** FIS-0003 already proposed Plumtree eager/lazy digest gossip for this exact path. This entry does NOT re-propose it — it **narrows FIS-0003 to the one slice that pays off at home-mesh scale (the idle heartbeat), makes the digest concrete (reuse `state_root_hex`-shaped identity, not a new hash), adds a second independent win FIS-0003 didn't cover (conditional bundle-pull), and hardens both against an adversarial review that found three real holes.** Plumtree's eager/lazy *tree topology* stays deferred to FIS-0003's scope (only matters at dozens of peers).

- **Grounded problem statement — two corrections to the brief `[verified: own-tools]`:**
  1. The 30s remint is **not unconditional**: `maybe_mint_and_broadcast` (gossip_runtime.rs:278+) early-returns unless `candidates_changed || timer_elapsed`. And the bundle is the **endpoint-candidate `GossipBundle`** (`mint_bundle_with_timestamp(signing_key, seq, now, candidates)`), not the membership bundle. The real inefficiency is sharper than the brief stated: on every idle 30s heartbeat the node mints a **brand-new signed bundle with a fresh sequence** — one Ed25519 signing op, one fail-closed **watermark disk persist** (write BEFORE broadcast, gossip_runtime.rs doc comment), then a full-bundle push (≤705B, 4KiB-capped) to every peer — purely to say "nothing changed." The heartbeat's stated purpose (doc comment :65-72) is bounded-window delivery to peers that joined after the last mint.
  2. This subsystem is still **wired-but-unattached in production** (`attach_gossip_runtime`: zero callers beyond its definition, a comment, and the lab-state MCP's own "wired-but-not-yet-daemon-integrated" string, `lab_state.rs:4377` `[verified: own-tools]`). So this is a design that slots into that frame when D2.7 wiring lands — it does not alter shipped behavior, and its savings are prospective. The anchor bundle-pull path (part 2) IS live.

- **The digest scheme (concrete):**
  - **Gossip heartbeat replacement.** The idle-heartbeat branch (`timer_elapsed && !candidates_changed`) no longer mints/signs/persists/pushes a full bundle. Instead it pushes a tiny **unsigned** `GossipIHave { source_node_id: [u8;32], sequence: u64 }` (40B) to each peer — the source's already-known last-minted sequence, which is exactly the value the receiver's monotonic watermark is keyed on. No new signing op, no new sequence, no watermark disk write (the heartbeat carries no new state). Rules, unchanged from FIS-0003's invariant that digests never gate trust: **(R1)** a receiver NEVER advances its watermark from an IHAVE — only the full-bundle accept pipeline (`accept_bundle_with_now`: Ed25519 sig → freshness → strict-monotonic sequence → revoked-source) does; **(R2)** IHAVE `sequence <= watermark` → ignored; **(R3)** IHAVE `sequence > watermark` → a rate-limited `GossipGraft { source_node_id }` back to the sender, which replies with its cached last-minted full bundle, which then runs the unchanged accept pipeline; **(R4)** a real candidate CHANGE still eagerly pushes the full signed bundle immediately, exactly as today — the digest only replaces the idle heartbeat, and the eager-push path is never gated on any digest state; **(R5)** mixed-version compat: a peer receives digest heartbeats only after it has itself sent us an IHAVE at least once (proving it speaks the protocol); until then it gets full-bundle heartbeats byte-identically to today.
  - **Why `state_root_hex` is NOT the gossip digest, despite the brief's steer:** the gossip bundle is endpoint candidates, whose freshness is already a per-source monotonic **sequence** — a `u64` is a cheaper, already-authoritative "have you seen up to here" digest than re-hashing the payload, and it is what the accept pipeline already compares. `state_root_hex` is the right digest for the *membership* state (part 2), where the discriminator is content-identity, not a sequence.
  - **Conditional membership bundle-pull (the new, live win).** The anchor bundle-pull is a TCP request: client sends `<token>\n`, server replies `OK <len>\n<bundle>` or `ERR unauthorized\n` (`write_anchor_bundle_pull_response`, daemon.rs:1004-1023 `[verified: own-tools]`). Amendment: the client MAY send a second line `have <epoch> <state_root_hex>` after the token. A NEW server whose current membership bundle matches replies `UNCHANGED\n` (a hash-sized round trip instead of the full 300-450B signed bundle). Backward compat: an OLD server never reads the second line and always sends the full bundle; an OLD client never sends it. `state_root_hex` is the correct digest here — it is `sha256(canonical_payload(state))`, already computed on every apply as the epoch-chain integrity check (FIS-0019 `[verified: own-tools, prior pass]`), covering the full state, so equality is exact-state equality.

- **Adversarial review outcome (§5e) — three real holes found, all now addressed `[reviewed: native-subagent]`:**
  1. **Silent-drop liveness regression (moderate, the sharpest gossip finding).** Today's unconditional full heartbeat is authenticated proof-of-liveness every 30s. Under digest-only heartbeats, an on-path attacker who drops ONLY the 40B IHAVE packets (cheap, pattern-matchable) for a source whose candidates aren't changing suppresses that liveness refresh indefinitely, with no escalation — there was no gossip-side analog of the bundle-pull backstop. **Fix folded in: a hard floor — even with digests active, re-mint and full-push a signed bundle at least every Kth heartbeat (K=5 ⇒ ≤150s), unconditionally.** Restores a bounded-latency authenticated-liveness guarantee while keeping ~80% of the idle-heartbeat savings.
  2. **Unsigned-IHAVE identity binding (the root of two holes).** GRAFT routing (R3) and the R5 "has this peer sent an IHAVE" capability flag must be bound to the **authenticated transport-session peer identity**, never to the `source_node_id` field inside the unsigned IHAVE. Otherwise a single forged IHAVE could (a) redirect a GRAFT or (b) flip a legitimate old-style peer into "digest-capable," after which it silently stops getting heartbeats it can parse. **Fix folded in as a numbered acceptance criterion: IHAVE's payload identity is used only to name the source being summarized; GRAFT destination and capability-observation are bound to the connection's authenticated peer.** (Whatever comes back still runs the full accept pipeline, so no forgery of *content* is possible regardless — this only closes the suppression/redirect surface.)
  3. **UNCHANGED silent-withholding window (bounded).** A lying/MITM'd `UNCHANGED` can delay (never forge/rollback — the guard chain still applies to any bundle that arrives). **Fix folded in: (a) the client forces an unconditional full pull every Nth pull (N=10) via a pure client-local monotonic counter that no server response may reset or influence — stated as a MUST; (b) the counter bounds silent staleness to ≤N cycles.** The review's honest caveat is recorded: this trades today's *loud* withholding (refusal/error, visible to monitoring) for a *silent* bounded one — acceptable given the guard chain, but operators keying alerts on pull failures should know.

- **Why it's actually better (quantified, honest about scale):** a full idle heartbeat is a sign + a disk fsync + ≤705B×peers; the digest is 40B×peers with no sign/fsync. At the home-mesh common case (3-5 peers) the bandwidth delta is tens of bytes/heartbeat — **the real per-node win is eliminating the signing + fail-closed disk persist on every idle 30s tick**, which matters on a Pi-class anchor, not the wire bytes. At 20-50 peers the wire savings compound (40B vs ≤705B × N, minus the 1-in-5 full backstop). Bundle-pull `UNCHANGED` saves ~300-450B → ~70B per unchanged pull, meaningful for a mobile client polling a busy anchor. Honest: at 3 peers this is a headroom/elegance + Pi-CPU improvement, not a fix for an active resource problem — same finding as FIS-0003's self-assessment.

- **Cost / tradeoffs:** new wire types `GossipIHave`/`GossipGraft` (40B unsigned, inside the existing 4KiB UDP cap, same port); a per-peer `last_seen_ihave` capability bit + a graft-responder token bucket; the bundle-pull `have`/`UNCHANGED` line pair. New failure modes are the three the review surfaced, each with its fix above. Net new code is moderate (roughly the accept-path size again) — not a small patch; Phase 1 (below) is the cheap, independently-valuable slice.

- **Ground-rules check (§A2):** no new forgery/downgrade surface — PASS with the two review fixes (R1 keeps digests non-authoritative; identity binding closes the forged-IHAVE holes; fail-toward-full-bundle on any doubt via R3 + the K-heartbeat backstop). Anti-replay/epoch unchanged — PASS (the accept pipeline and the membership apply guard chain are untouched). Graceful mixed-version degradation — PASS (R5 for gossip; old-server/old-client fall-through for bundle-pull). Cheaper than sending the full bundle — PASS (40B + no sign/fsync vs ≤705B + sign + fsync). Safe Rust — PASS.

- **What would falsify it:** a live-lab drop-only test where digest-mode liveness is worse than today's despite the K-heartbeat backstop (would mean K is too large); or measurement showing the signing+fsync elimination is negligible on target hardware (would collapse the small-scale rationale to bandwidth-only, i.e. FIS-0003 territory — ship the bundle-pull half only); or any interleaving where the guard chain accepts a digest-suppressed stale bundle (would be a hard reject — but R1 makes this structurally impossible).

- **Prior art:** Dynamo/Cassandra anti-entropy (exchange a digest, diff, sync) — the bundle-pull `have`/`UNCHANGED` is exactly this. Plumtree (Leitão et al., SRDS 2007) eager-push + lazy IHAVE/GRAFT — the gossip heartbeat's R1-R5, deferring the tree topology to FIS-0003. SWIM (Das et al., DSN 2002) piggyback-on-heartbeat liveness — the K-heartbeat backstop is the liveness half the review showed the digest must preserve.

- **Detailed Recommended Patch Implementation Plan:**
  - **New types:** `GossipIHave { source_node_id: [u8;32], sequence: u64 }`, `GossipGraft { source_node_id: [u8;32] }` (peer_gossip.rs wire, new variant tags); `GossipNode` gains `HashMap<[u8;32] /* authenticated peer */, PeerDigestState { supports_digest: bool, heartbeats_since_full: u8 }>` and a per-source graft-responder token bucket; bundle-pull gains a `have`-line parser + `UNCHANGED` response arm.
  - **Modified fns:** `maybe_mint_and_broadcast` (gossip_runtime.rs) — idle branch emits IHAVE unless `heartbeats_since_full >= K`, else full-push-and-reset; new `ingest_ihave`/`ingest_graft` handlers; `write_anchor_bundle_pull_response` (daemon.rs:1004) + `read_anchor_bundle_pull_request_token` (daemon.rs:1058) extended for the optional line; the pull client gains the monotonic force-full counter.
  - **Existing tests that must keep passing (find + name before touching):** the gossip three-peer mesh test (`tests/gossip_three_peer_mesh.rs`), `accept_bundle_with_now` rejection-path tests, and the anchor bundle-pull token tests around `write_anchor_bundle_pull_response`/`read_anchor_bundle_pull_request_token` `[verified: own-tools — these functions exist; exact test names to be enumerated at patch time]`.
  - **New tests:** `ihave_never_advances_watermark`; `stale_ihave_ignored`; `higher_ihave_triggers_rate_limited_graft`; `graft_response_still_runs_full_accept_pipeline`; `forged_ihave_cannot_redirect_graft_or_flip_capability` (identity binding); `kth_heartbeat_forces_full_bundle_under_digest` (liveness backstop); `mixed_version_peer_without_ihave_gets_full_heartbeats` (R5); bundle-pull `unchanged_response_on_matching_state_root`, `old_client_never_sends_have_line`, `old_server_ignores_have_line`, `forced_full_pull_counter_immune_to_unchanged`.
  - **Commit sequence + effort:** 1 (S) conditional bundle-pull (`have`/`UNCHANGED` + forced-full counter + tests) — LIVE path, independently valuable, no gossip-attachment dependency; 2 (M) `GossipIHave`/`GossipGraft` types + handlers + token bucket, all peers default full-push (behavior-identical); 3 (M) idle-heartbeat digest switch + K-heartbeat backstop + R5 capability gate + identity binding; 4 (S) mixed-version + drop-resistance live-lab stage once D2.7 attachment lands. Total S-M-M-S.

## FIS-0021: Review-hardened hysteresis for continuous path-quality migration (a FIS-0013 hardening delta)

- **Pipeline / area:** `crates/rustynetd/src/traversal.rs` + `daemon.rs` path-quality tracker + `rustynet-backend-wireguard` userspace-shared engine (the two discarded `(_loss, _rtt)` sites). Path-selection intelligence only.

- **Relationship to FIS-0013:** FIS-0013 (this same document, 2026-07-02) already did the heavy design for Part B — it un-discards `loss`/`rtt` at `engine.rs:345/:531` behind a primitive-only `PeerPathSample` trait method, resolved the shadow-probe question (dropped it — the engine drops unmatched-source datagrams pre-crypto and is a `supports_roaming: false` single-endpoint slot, so migration = flip-the-slot + require-authenticated-handshake, with the existing 30s staleness re-race as recovery), and specified EWMA + fixed-margin + dwell hysteresis. **This entry does not re-propose that. It is a focused hardening delta: FIS-0013's exact thresholds went to adversarial flapping review (§5f) and it found three concrete oscillation/soundness gaps that FIS-0013's numbers did not close.** Everything else in FIS-0013 (measurement plumbing, trait shape, migration↔recovery reuse, FIS-0010 breaker precedence) stands; apply these deltas on top before Phase 4 (gated migration).

- **Grounded problem statement `[verified: own-tools]`:** both `tunnel.stats()` sites still discard `(_loss, _rtt)` at `engine.rs:345` (engine-wide aggregate) and `:531` (`authenticated_handshake_unix`, a per-packet path — corrected in FIS-0013); no other reader of loss/rtt exists in the workspace (`grep last_rtt|estimate_loss` outside `third_party` = only these two sites `[verified: own-tools]`). Path selection still happens once at connect via the ICE pair-race and is never re-scored while a healthy path holds. The FIS-0013 base design reads the signal at the ~1s reconcile tick and migrates by re-programming the single endpoint slot.

- **The three review-driven hardening deltas (§5f) `[reviewed: native-subagent]`:**
  1. **Migration effectiveness gate (closes the biggest gap).** The review's sharpest finding: a migration that *completes its handshake within 10s* is treated as success, but handshake-completion says nothing about sustained loss/RTT on the new path — so a flap between two simultaneously-bad candidates (symmetric shared-medium interference, or an end-host radio problem misdiagnosed as a path problem) sails through, and quarantine (keyed on migration *failure*) never engages. **Delta: a migrated-to path is not "confirmed" — and the next flip is not eligible — until it has been observed good (loss_ewma below threshold, fresh handshake) for a **post-migration verification window (30s / ≥10 consecutive good 1s polls)**. A migration whose target fails verification counts as a failed migration: it trips quarantine (900s) and feeds the FIS-0010 breaker, exactly like a handshake failure.** This converts the review's "clocked flapping at the dwell cadence" into "one attempt, then the target is quarantined and the breaker opens."
  2. **`srtt_slow` baseline drift cap.** FIS-0013's slow baseline used a fixed `alpha=1/64` (~2h time constant). The review showed one fixed constant can't serve two jobs: on a step change (roaming) the fast `srtt` crosses `2*srtt_slow` for hours before the baseline absorbs it → a multi-hour flap window; and a slow-boiling degradation (RTT creeping up slower than the baseline absorbs) never trips the `2×` trigger at all → missed detection. **Delta: cap `srtt_slow` absorption rate (e.g. ≤20ms/hour movement) so a genuine step change is absorbed in bounded time without a multi-hour flap window, and slow degradation still eventually crosses the relative gate.** The `2×` relative arm keeps the `+50ms` absolute co-requirement from FIS-0013 (a 5→11ms LAN blip still can't trigger).
  3. **Freshness-gate field split (a soundness trap).** FIS-0013's "verdict Insufficient unless last sample age ≤ 10s" is ambiguous and, taken literally (age of *any* 1s poll), is **vacuous** — a loss-only poll refreshes it every second, so an 8-minute-stale `srtt` still passes the gate. **Delta: split into `last_poll_age` (liveness of the sampler) and `last_rtt_sample_age` (recency of an actual RTT ingest), and gate the RTT arm specifically on `last_rtt_sample_age`, with a threshold sized to RTT's ~120s cadence (≤180-240s, "at most one missed handshake stale"), NOT 10s.** The 10s figure was a unit mismatch against a 120s-cadence signal. Loss-arm freshness stays on the 1s poll.
  Plus the review's fourth, confirmatory point, adopted: **the FIS-0010 breaker must be keyed per-(peer, candidate-pair), not only by direct↔relay transition type** — otherwise a symmetric direct-A↔direct-B flap generates no direct↔relay failures and runs unthrottled except by dwell. FIS-0013 delegated breaker semantics to FIS-0010; this pins the required key granularity.

- **The scoring function (FIS-0013 base, unchanged):** `loss_ewma ← 0.75·loss_ewma + 0.25·loss_sample` per 1s poll (light re-smoothing of boringtun's already-session-weighted estimate — the review flagged this double-smoothing lengthens effective reaction time, which the verification gate now tolerates because a real migration is only committed after sustained evidence, not a single fast crossing); SRTT/RTTVAR with RFC 6298 α=1/8, β=1/4 (smoothing constants only), `srtt_slow` α=1/64 **with the drift cap above**. Degraded iff sustained: loss arm `loss_ewma ≥ 0.05` for 5 consecutive polls; rtt arm `srtt ≥ 2·srtt_slow AND srtt−srtt_slow ≥ 50ms` for 2 consecutive fresh handshake samples. Action gated on: dwell ≥ 300s since last migration, breaker Closed (per-pair), AND — new — no unconfirmed prior migration in flight.

- **Why it's actually better / the failure it fixes:** today a Direct path that has quietly degraded to 15% loss but still handshakes is never reconsidered until it fully dies. The base FIS-0013 mechanism migrates proactively; these deltas ensure it does so **without trading that for a new flapping failure mode** — the review demonstrated that FIS-0013's dwell-only damping still permits sustained clocked oscillation under realistic shared-medium interference, and the verification gate + per-pair breaker + quarantine-on-ineffective-migration close it.

- **Ground-rules check (§B2):** no new probe traffic — PASS (reads existing handshake/keepalive-driven stats only). Hysteresis concrete and flap-proof — PASS, materially strengthened by the three deltas (this is the whole point of the pass). Migration doesn't create a stale/duplicate authoritative path — PASS (single-endpoint-slot flip, WireGuard session keys survive, authenticated-handshake-gated commit, existing re-race recovers — all per FIS-0013's verified trace of the phase10 commit path). Safe Rust, cross-platform mirror — PASS (measurement lands once in shared engine.rs; macOS runtime request variant mirrored, per FIS-0013).

- **What would falsify it:** a live-lab tc-netem run with symmetric ~2-3min-period loss bursts on both candidates showing >1 migration/hour despite the verification gate + quarantine (would mean the verification window is too short or quarantine too brief); or a boiling-frog RTT ramp that the drift-capped baseline still never detects (would mean the cap is too loose); or the freshness split still admitting an 8-min-stale srtt into a migration decision (would mean the gate wiring regressed to the vacuous reading).

- **Prior art:** QUIC connection migration (RFC 9000 §9) validate-before-commit — the migration-effectiveness gate extends this from "path validated" to "path validated AND sustained-good." Tailscale magicsock continuous re-evaluation. Jacobson/Karels + RFC 6298 for the SRTT/RTTVAR smoothing constants only. The review's finding maps to classic cascaded-low-pass overshoot: two smoothing filters in series (session-EWMA then poll-EWMA) add phase lag, which the sustained-evidence gates absorb.

- **Detailed Recommended Patch Implementation Plan (delta on top of FIS-0013's plan):**
  - **Modified structs:** FIS-0013's `PathQualityState` gains `last_rtt_sample_age`/`last_poll_age` split, `srtt_slow` drift-cap bookkeeping, and a `pending_verification: Option<{ candidate, good_polls: u8, deadline }>`; a per-peer `quarantine: HashMap<Candidate, expiry_unix>`.
  - **Modified fns:** the reconcile-tick verdict fn gates on `last_rtt_sample_age` for the RTT arm; the migration commit path enters `pending_verification` rather than declaring success on handshake; a new verification-poll step promotes or quarantines-and-breaks; breaker interaction keyed per-(peer,candidate-pair).
  - **Existing tests that must keep passing:** FIS-0013's named set (phase10 traversal-probe tests :10545-:10917, daemon `…periodic_reprobe…`/`…direct_health…` tests, the backend stats/handshake tests) — all take the migration feature-flag off / verification-gate absent ⇒ unchanged.
  - **New tests (flapping-resistance, using the reviewed numbers):** `symmetric_degradation_migrates_at_most_once_then_quarantines` (the review's exact scenario — both candidates bad on a 2-3min cadence; assert ≤1 migration then breaker-open); `ineffective_migration_trips_quarantine_and_breaker`; `srtt_slow_drift_cap_bounds_step_change_flap_window`; `boiling_frog_rtt_ramp_eventually_triggers`; `rtt_arm_gated_on_rtt_sample_age_not_poll_age` (freeze RTT ingest, keep loss polling, assert Insufficient); `post_migration_verification_window_blocks_immediate_reflip`.
  - **Commit sequence + effort:** slots between FIS-0013's Phase 3 (shadow-mode) and Phase 4 (gated migration): 1 (S) freshness-gate field split + its test (pure correctness, no behavior change); 2 (S) srtt_slow drift cap + tests; 3 (M) migration-effectiveness verification gate + quarantine + per-pair breaker key + the flapping-resistance suite; 4 (M, lab) the tc-netem symmetric-degradation stage as the Phase-4 sign-off gate. Total S-S-M-M.

## Focused pass — Considered and rejected (gossip + path quality)

- **`state_root_hex` as the GOSSIP digest** — rejected: the gossip bundle's freshness discriminator is an already-authoritative per-source monotonic `u64` sequence; a `u64` is cheaper and is exactly what the accept pipeline already compares. `state_root_hex` is used where it belongs — as the *membership* bundle-pull digest, where the discriminator is content-identity. `[reviewed: native-subagent]` concurred this is the right split.
- **Plumtree eager/lazy TREE topology in this pass** — deferred to FIS-0003 (its home); the tree only pays at dozens of peers, out of scope for a home-mesh-scale efficiency slice. Only the IHAVE/GRAFT idle-heartbeat digest is adopted here.
- **Signing the IHAVE digest** — rejected: signing every heartbeat is the cost this pass removes; keeping IHAVE unsigned is sound because R1 makes it non-authoritative and the identity-binding fix (review hole #2) closes the only suppression surface an unsigned hint opens.
- **FIS-0013's dwell-only damping as sufficient** — rejected by §5f review: it permits sustained clocked flapping under realistic symmetric interference. The verification gate + per-pair breaker + quarantine-on-ineffective-migration are the minimum additions that close it; a naive "just lengthen the dwell" was considered and rejected (it slows legitimate migrations without stopping beat-frequency oscillation).
- **A dedicated path-quality heartbeat/ping** — out of scope per §B2 (a separately-justified proposal); this pass reads only existing handshake/keepalive-driven stats.

## Focused pass — Coverage note (gossip + path quality)

- **External review path:** both provisioned HTTPS vendors (ZenMux DeepSeek, NaraRouter Mistral — the deliberately-different second family) were unreachable from this sandbox (curl status 000 for both, before any token was sent), so §5e/§5f ran on the sanctioned last-resort native-subagent path and are tagged `[reviewed: native-subagent]` throughout — a genuinely independent adversarial pass, but same model family, not the cross-vendor diversity the charter preferred. Both reviews found real, addressed holes (three each), incorporated above rather than buried.
- The gossip subsystem's production-attachment gap (`attach_gossip_runtime` unwired) means FIS-0020's gossip half cannot be live-lab-proven until D2.7 lands; the bundle-pull half is live now. This gap is a prerequisite, not solved here.
- FIS-0021 leans on FIS-0013's first-hand trace of the phase10 migration commit path (single-slot flip, session-survival, re-race recovery) rather than re-verifying it this pass — flagged as `[verified: own-tools, prior pass FIS-0013]` where relied upon; a fresh reviewer should re-confirm before Phase 4.
- Exact existing-test names for FIS-0020's gossip/bundle-pull "must keep passing" set were located by function, not enumerated by test name this pass (budget) — a patch-time step.
- Method: four own-tools checks (maybe_mint_and_broadcast full read; heartbeat cost shape; the two stats() sites + repo-wide loss/rtt reader sweep; bundle-pull protocol shape) + two native-subagent adversarial reviews. `b79cac1` tree confirmed byte-identical to `5868a09`; line numbers verified 2026-07-02, they will drift.

  relay selection): both are wire-format changes with open protocol
  questions recorded in the grounding notes — `RelayHelloAck` today has only
  `session_id` + `allocated_port` (`rustynet-relay/src/transport.rs`), so
  `version`/`hello_interval_secs` must be designed in before `load_hint`;
  `DnsZoneRecord` has eight fields of which only `target_node_id` changes;
  the unsigned beacon needs a NEW UDP port plus per-OS firewall rules.
  Deferred whole rather than landed rushed.
